O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, dear sons, I have completed this book, which is the summary of medical science, in its entirety; and I have brought it to an end through its explanations and declaratory sentences.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete this treatise with you, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say, "surgery.
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is done in our region and is strange from all sides, it is a difficult science and requires little time compared to the small descriptions in books of ancient authors that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And because there has come error and vanity, and intentions are closed, and the science is alienated.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	For it seems to me that I will revive this treatise with the arrangement of this treatise according to the way of explanations and declarations and abbreviations; and I will come together with the forms of the cautery instruments, and other tools of the work, with the preparation and arrangement thereof, as is fitting.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that good masters of hands are not found in our land, the art of medicine is prolonged.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who deals with it must master the science of anatomy, as Galen says, until he knows the shape and form and joining together and separation of the bones, and is aware of the nerves and joints and ligaments and the number of joints, and the movement and flow of veins and the rest and birth of limbs.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason, as Hipocrates says, what is good with one hand is bad with the other, and what is good to do with one hand is bad to do with the hand that holds it; and most of all in the art of the hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	Now we tell you in the introduction of this book that whoever is not acquainted with the above-mentioned things should be careful not to make mistakes and not to harm people; so I have often wished that many of those who deal with this science would abandon their knowledge and lack of experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	I saw a fool of a man who cut an abscess from the scrofula on the neck of a woman, and he cut the arteries of her neck; for so much blood flowed out that the woman died in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another fool who tried to cut a stone out of a man's bladder, and the stone was large; he took a piece of the bladder with him, and he died in three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already seen one who was called in to treat it, and saw the condition of the patient and the size of the stone; and if he tried to treat him, he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another fool who took in our duke's leg which was broken, and with the break there was a wound; and the ignorant doctor pulled the break on the wound to the point of pain, and left it without a bandage, and left it so; and he ordered that it not be removed; and it delayed until the whole leg became gangrened, and came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to go to him, and I hurried to dislocate the leg; and when I did so, he was in peace and felt no pain at all.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But any way that corruption came to the member, and it could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease to go through the member until all members were lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another wonder that broke out into an abscess filled with putrefaction, and then Inflamed by the evil of its own virulence.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For chancres, when they are purifying with melancholy humor, come not except that one touch them with iron if it is not in the right place where one can entirely cut off what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this, very fine children, you should know that the work of the hands is divided into two divisions: namely, those in which there is danger in many ways; and I will show in each of these in this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For for that it is needed that you keep them, so that the young man does not speak ill of you; if you take your weapons in harmony, and undertake your patients lightly but firmly, and use the better way so that through the grace of God you come to salvation and be free; and leave behind probable diseases of grief health; and hold your weapons from him who makes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galiën said in some of his admonitions: "Do not take on the care of a bad disease, lest you be called a fool.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire cauterizations and water-based medicine, and the order of the limbs; and the forms of instruments, and the tools for cauterization, and all that is necessary in this work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters are of dislocation and the tools for it, suction cups and wounds, extraction of arrows, and similar things; and the chapters are ordered and the shapes of the instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapters are about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is ordered that the heads of the tools be cut off as soon as possible, and the shapes of the instruments are given.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus we remember the work, it is necessary that I give the quality of the help and the harm of each color.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of help and harm is the longest word and subtlest science and the most complex answers; and many wise men would speak on this, and agree with it; and I am short on words because I shorten them.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the universal help of all colors or matter, except for two types of color: that is to say, hot color with matter and dry color with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry complexions together matter, some devised and said that cautery is great help; and the other said the opposite: that cautery does not worth to diseases that come from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire if it is hot, and should not be cured by hot disease from heat, nor by dryness; and he who said that cautery makes great help to hot and dry disease which comes in courses of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of the man and his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it never once by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And all way, nothing is as good for it as he who has experienced it, and who knows by long use the paste of cauteries, and the diversity of complexions of men, and their dispositions and causes of their diseases, and the season and space thereof; of other complexions we have no fear, even if it be a cold and moist disease.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all of them were to come together and agree with the fire cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, children, that fire cautery is better if it comes out of the cure, and of greater goodness than medical fire cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and comes only to the member that is cooked, and does not harm another member at all.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The burning medicines come from one member to another by removal, and cause disease of great healing; and perhaps fire, because of its height and the goodness of its substance, does not hurt if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And what I have found by experiment and through the length of service and study that I have put into this art, and is based on the truth of things; and because I am sorry for the length of speech, for it does not please me to keep you from the secret which has been answered in fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives away diseases from the body, as the philosopher says in demonstrating; take it into your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that it is necessary to agree on what time should be used for the fire cauterization, and let them be made.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is appropriate in all seasons, because the harm that may arise is prevented by the aid of cauterization; and most especially, the cauterization is for necessary pains that cannot be waited for the time when greater grief may come to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And I do not think at all, dear son, as they say the foolish people; for with the illness that is cured by cauterization there is no return; and it serves thus: but it is not so as they think, because cauterization is nothing more than a medicine that changes the appearance, dries up the humors that cause pain, and is worth more as a medicine due to its quick effect, and for its virtue and excellence.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And a possible thing is that the disease comes according to the complexion of the patient and the place of the illness and its virtue; and excesses are assembled in him by acquiring meat and similar things, unless fire cauterization is administered at the place where he has little surplus and moisture, as with fire cauterization for pain, and similar things, and partial pain does not return again; but that happens a little.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	And so open well that the cauterization is of medicine, not because of the intention of foolish doctors.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that the cauterization instrument of gold is more healing than that of iron, and they said that fire-iron was only used because of its quality of gold and for its high substance; and they said that the heat of the cauterization does not cause pustules, but this is not true because I have tried it, and found that it is true in some people; and a cauterization of gold is more healing than iron, as they said.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And moreover when you heat the gold instrument, you are not so when it is heated by the color of gold, and it soon cools down; and if you heat it too much, it will go into the fire, and in this way there is enough impediment.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this we use fire cauterization, which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	For in this chapter on the treatment of headaches, I will instruct you on how to do it correctly so that it is easier for you to find the right spot.
dou cautere olivaire	The olive oil cauterization
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	The olive oil cauterization: For the treatment of headaches and the relief of pain in the head, ears, and teeth due to various causes, including cold and湿气/humors (i.e., excess moisture or dampness), as well as many other diseases caused by cold, such as paralysis, lameness, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The method for this cauterization is as follows: The treatment for the headache and pain in the head, ears, and teeth should be done with a medicine that dissolves and washes away the head pains or three [3] or four [4] times, depending on the nature of the disease and the patient's tolerance and custom. Then, re-apply to the patient's head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then place the fire on the cross between your hands, and put his hands on his chest; after that put the root of your palm on the root of his neck between its two eyes; and leave the two hands come, so it bleeds from the nose then heat the fire called "oliver", which is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then place the fire on the cross between your hands, and put his hands on his chest; after that put the root of your palm on the root of his neck between its two eyes; and leave the two hands come, so it bleeds from the nose then heat the fire called "oliver", which is the form: And let it rest in ink for a while, and slowly extract your hand again and again; then release your hand completely, and find the small bone at the top; and if you don't see it, then restart the fire until you see the bone as I told you; after that take a piece of string, and put cotton wet and soft inside, and put on the fire, and let it be there for three days; after that put cotton drenched in oil inside; and let it be there until it burns; then treat the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmacon" until it heals.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And they said to me, The longer the wound remains open, the more it will suppurate; and for this reason if it is healed with a poultice.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they said to me: Let the cautery remain applied so long that part of the bone be burned; and then remove what is burned from the bone, and let it be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And another said to me: Let the cautery remain applied so long that it burns as far as the bone, and then remove it as far as the humor comes out; and one should let the wound remain open for a long time; afterwards one should cure and dress it.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two methods of applying the fire seem good to me neither for all nor for all men; and they seem to me that I should let it remain applied; for the head is weakened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we testify in other limbs; and yet more so when the head of the sick person is weak by nature, and the first impression of the fire seems good to me and gives a sort of relief, and I use it in such a way that it seems salutary.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When all the head comes to chronic pain and lasts a long time, then use herbs and pills called "cochier" and head purgation and oils and plasters; and if you do the fire cautery that we have just mentioned, and it does not work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that the head of the patient is of a strong nature, and that he is not too cold; then cauterize him slightly as we have just mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After you have made the fire cautery on each horn of the head as we have just mentioned, and you have made the cauterization at the root called "vasselz"; and place the cupping vessels; and adjust your hand so that you do not see the bone: the patient will feel a lot more intense pain during this cauterization than during others, which I will speak about later; and it is right that the cornes cauterizations be smaller than those with which we cauterize the hair of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	Dou cautere dou chief
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in one part of the head comes sudden pain and is stretched out to the oil, and the head is purged with medicinal herbs, and other cures have been done as I said in the division of diseases, and none of them profit: then make cauterization according to two ways, that is to say, with medicinal water and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The fire cautery: If you squeeze a little bottle of oil, and peel off the skin and re-apply it to the wound at the base, and then let it rest for twelve hours or more; and then release it and treat with garlic, and leave the wound for two or three days; and then put cotton dipped in wax on it until it heals.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the cure of injury as long as it is healthy; and if you see that this one of some burning medicines that I have written or dosed in the treatment of burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery, if it is done in this way.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cautery so that it is hot:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And call it "close" because the head is made in the form of a clod or there is I little curve, and in the middle to a small appearance; and put it on the painful place, and hold your hand and turn the fire slightly, until half of the pain of the keur is burned; and remove your hand that the artery does not burn, which is gone, and runs a lot of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After put cotton in silk, and put it on the place for three days; then I put moistened cotton in butter, and then cure the place of injury as long as it is healthy; and if you want to cauterize this headache with the cautery that is called "cutelare", all over its tip, and be careful not to plug the artery in this headache which is not old.
de emigraine	of headaches
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat headaches as we have already said in the division of diseases, and do not benefit from it, and see that the cauterization before mentioned with medicine and iron does not suit him, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery which is called "cultellare" until it is white; and thus sign over the place of pain a line half a inch long, and hold your hand there once, and draw back so that you do not cover the artery and do not come up to the bone; and guard against the mandible that moves when you chew, and let the rustiness of the blood of the artery remain that it may be drawn back, or drawing back give great fear and especially to one who does not know it, and who is a student and untried; and leave the work half done; but I will tell you how to stop bleeding when the artery is clamped, and I will show you where it happens in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	Et si tu vois que ce cautère ne suffit pas à la maladie, et que le patient souffre, appliquez le cautère au niveau du cou comme nous l'avons dit, et guérir la plaie jusqu'à ce qu'elle soit saine; et si tu vois, administre le cautère que nous avons dit ou chapastre de l'extraction de l'artère, avec le cautère qui a deux coutelz; et c'est ce cautère est meilleurs de celui et plus aidants.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	And if you see that this cautery does not suffice to the disease, and the patient suffers, apply the cautery at the level of the neck as we have said, and cure the wound until it is well; and if you see, administer the cautery that we have said or chapastre of the extraction of the artery, with the cautery which has two blades; and this cautery is better than that and more helpful.
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When there is pain in the ear from cold, and one has applied liquid medicines and other treatments that we have mentioned in the division, and the pain does not cease, then heat this cautery which is called "poins", of which form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After piercing all around the painful ear, where it hurts on both sides, and moving away a little from the root of the ear since you have found the place of pain; and having pierced each ear nine times; after that treat the place until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the mouth torture
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	torture must be cured by cautery is only effective for those that move with fluid, as we said in the division of diseases; and not to do any cauterization on the similarities that come from dryness and waste of heat.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this torture of fluid movement from the throat and gargling and spitting, and this does not help, then it is appropriate that you cauterize the pain in three places: one at the root of the ear, and another a little farther away from the temple, and the third between the lips; and apply the cauterium to the part which should be cured until half of it has burned; and this is the form of the cauterium:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the appearance of the surgical knife that we have put before you is a little more subtle and it is necessary for the knives to be a little larger; after the treatment, take care of the wound as I said above until it is well.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it as we have said, it does not help, and the patient has no fever, then do four cauterizations: II on the two horns of the head, and I cut off the head, and I cauterize what is called "vessel" as we have said before, and then cauterize behind the mouth of the stomach; and treat it as we have said above.
de litargie	of lime
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	This is a disease that requires the patient to take large pills and pour oil on the brain; after cutting off the head of the patient completely, and putting on the occiput the resin of saffron which is written or used for making plasters; and this is the way of cauterization: do so as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is healthy then it is good; and if it is not, three fire cauterizations on the head at the base, with two-inch space between each, and two ounces of gros in the middle; and cure as for others, and if he twitches, the patient suffers, one cauterization in the middle; and it is necessary to make two others on the two horns, and cure until it is healthy; and let the cauterizations which are called 'olive' be made as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be washed and that what we have said before be followed; then the head of the patient is cauterized, and one cauterization on each horn, one behind and three on the spine at the back of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is moist and the patient suffers, and the disease persists, then three cauterizations are made on the spine at the base of the spine; and he leaves it until the fire on the last cauterization is extinguished, and he relaxes his hand; then the cure until it is healthy, and let the cauterizations which are called 'olive' be made as we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	Of epilepsy: One should not resort to fire cautery except for those who are febrile; it is necessary first to clean the skull and to administer other treatments that we have mentioned in the division when the disease is great and the patient suffers from fever.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	If it is a child who cannot bear the pain: make them gargle and chew, cleaning the skull often with good meat; then put the head in the middle, and apply the cautery according to what we have said above, and also on the neck and back spine, and treat as described for one who is paralyzed and has stiffening of the joints.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child: apply the subtle cautery according to this method:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy there are excess fluids or腐敗和厚密的湿润物，then half-heat cautery as we said before to the one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	When due to melancholy, there is a declining of excess fluids into melancholy, and the patient's body is moistened, then give him to drink something so that his brain may be purified, according to what is before it in division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After re-erecting the head of the patient; after making a well-formed turban out of linen, as well as a circle, place it on the head; and let the patient sit comfortably with his back well supported; then present the liniment, and dampen it with old almond butter; and heat it gently over fire so that he may bear it; after emptying the circle from inside the turban, and letting it cool; and do this to the patient every week once with another good government, until he is healed.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	And so you see how to cauterize him by making many punctures all over his body.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This method of cauterization moistens the skull and then puts cotton wetted with butter and linseed oil on it.
de l’awe des eulz	of the hair
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When it comes first to the hair by the signs that I have said in the division, then begin and do this to the patient purifying thing: wash or bath many times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After that he commands him to shave his head, and does the cauterization on his head, and does two cauterizations on the temples because they are desiccated: one where the hair is shaven and one where it remains; and be careful about the blood coming out, and if you see too much blood come out, then stop him with a cloth so that he doesn't burn himself.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in the incision of the cautery how to stop it; and no one does a cauterization or haematoma of the two hind bones.
dou cors des larmes	the cor of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and are on the veins, or extract the arteries which are in appearance at the top of the head; and one can see that it is the cold, phlegmatic, superfluous fluid, therefore let him do the cauterization I said at the beginning of the work descending to the eyes: I cauterize the top, and two cauterizations on the two temples, and two cauterizations where he haired out the two bones; and if it is necessary more, if he cauterizes bloodlessly above the eyebrow at every small cauterization.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	the cor of tears within the eyes

Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	This is the form of the cautery which is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the oil is softened by disease and moisture, then the cauterization with this cautery which is called "olive".
de coi ci est li forme:	from this is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that you do two cauteries on the two places as long as the hair are; and do not let your hand off until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the way I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	Dou hair that points to oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	No time has come when the hair of the oils is converted to the parched, and they pinch the oil, and one does cauterize according to two ways: that is to say, by fire, or by fiery medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they pinch at their base, hold them steady so that they do not move until they are born.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and are even, then put the patient in your care; then sign on the paper of the hairs a figure which is also like the fuel of the mirth, and is the beginning of the signature of the hairs; then put cotton wet in pitch and musk of persillion on the oil, then heat the cautery so that it is this form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After you have cauterized the wound little by little several times so that the scar is burned in place; and the sign of the health of the work is that you see the paper withdraw, and the hairs rise to the length of the oil; then lift your hand, and leave it like this for III days, then put cotton wet with ointment in the wound as long as the scarring is finished; after the healing care until he is healthy.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after that come the hairs, and the paper is softened then begin again the cauterizing on that middle point, as you did first; and if the hairs are missing, then cauterize until the paper is raised to its natural length, and even, and do not touch the hair oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The medical remedies are: that you command the patient to leave the hairs as long and even as they grow, then make of parchment the form of the leaf of Myrrh; then take of French soap and of hot salt, each a .Z., and grind them together well; and do it promptly, so that it does not cool down again, then pour on top of the parchment the eyes; and if the illness is in only one oil alone, then you must also work on the other side as well; and moisten with cotton the ointment wet in the jar; and the patient's joint shall be in your health and place your two fingers on the medicine, and press it little by little each time the patient feels the tingling of the medicine, for he feels the tingling as well as fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	Once you have finished, take the medicine to your mouth.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the medicine is over, take off the bandage and see if the paper has risen as if it had been lifted by fire or by incisions; and if so, then do well.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, put more medicine on the bandage where the medicine has not worked, until your hairs are even and at their tips; then put cotton wetted with burre on it as long as the sores burn, after treating the place that is called "dyafenis" and others, until they are well.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you need to, protect your wound from the medicine by a bandage so that it does not move away from the medicine by the hairs.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft again and the hairs grab at the oil, start the medicine on that same bandage that has been softened by the paper properly, just as you did before; after treating it until it is well; and this is the form of the medicine of lead:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are diverse in size and smallness, and according to what you should be restrained; and do not answer the right way to those who are subject to this craft.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the cure of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have said in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not benefit, then it is necessary that you apply cauterization according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place his head in your hands; and wipe his hair with a damp cloth or with juice of peppergrass on oil; then heat the cauterizer accordingly: and apply it to the hair at the base, so that it forms a little peak like the shape of a feather, join the two peaks together, and if you see any blood, let it flow; but certainly, the one who applies it must be careful for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	Aprés presse la fistule s'ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s'ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l'oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l'oil, et la corromp.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	After pressing the fistula, open it and treat the pus and dry it up; and if it is closed, then operate and cut deeply; after that, place a hot cauterizer firmly on the skin over the oil, and let your hand stay on the cauterizer over the affected area from above the oil, so that your hand does not go wild; and place the cauterizer in the grease of the oil, and corrupt it.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then restart the cauterization again once more, and if you need to do it again, leave it for III days; after that, put cotton wet in butter on it, and treat with drying medicine until it is healed, and if forty days have passed and it is not healed, then put corrosive medicine on it until the bone is uncovered; and follow up according to what came out in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way to cauterize a fistula which none of the ancients spoke of.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	When you see a fistula, cut it; then put in the cut a fine string so as to make it form:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and I have it at the amount of one .Z. of liquid; and hold your hand tightly so that the patient does not move, so that the melted liquid does not run to his oil; and you must put cotton moistened in alcohol on the oil at the base of the fistula, or on the skin: the liquid if it is well applied to the place of the fistula, and he heals with a wonderful health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	If the fistula is healed by the cautery that we have said, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then he should administer piercing to the nose, and bring back the fistula to the nose's own place according to what it is necessary in his own place.
des crevaices en levres	In the crevices of the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Mouths sometimes have crevices in the lips which are called "hair", and most often in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these crevices according to what we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, then heat a small surgical scalpel according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it firmly in the crevices as much as it will go; then cure with oil of wax until it is healed.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess from the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When the abscess comes up in the root of the throat or in the palate or at the roots of the teeth, after having made the pus run and it dries up and becomes a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in the divisions, and it does not help: then you must have the cautery according to the quantity of the fistula; after having sealed or pierced the fistula, and keep your hand until the iron comes out at the bottom of it, and do so once or twice, after treating as we have said in the treatment, until it is healed; and if it is healed in this way, it is good; and if not, then you must uncover the place and remove the rotted bone according to what you will find in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	Dou movement des dens.
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	The movement of the teeth. When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, treat it with medicines; this does not work, so put the head of the sick person in your lap; then heat the cautery until its form comes out like this in a certain way that you put a string on the tooth; and place the cautery very hot inside, and hold it for as long as your hand allows the sick person to feel the heat coming from the root of the tooth; then let go of your hand and start the cautery according to your will; then fill the mouth of the sick person with stale water, and leave it there for an hour and wash it thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	In this way, the tooth that was moving is stabilized, the gums are made firm, and the moisture that causes decay is dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of the teeth pain
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When the pain from cold comes with frostbite or there is cold and wet, and the remedies of medicines are not useful, then it is necessary to cauterize according to two ways: and cautery with butter and cautery with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery with butter: if it is such that you squeeze butter from a cow's udder, and the tip in a copper or bronze spoon; after take cotton and wrap it on the point of a needle, and the wet in butter, and put on the hurting tooth carefully and hold for as long as it cools down; and do this often until its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see the wool and cotton wet in butter, and put on the hurting tooth, and put on I bronze hot as long as the fire comes to the root of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Cautery with fire: if it is such that you squeeze a metal bar, copper or bronze, and it is thick so that the fire does not come to the mouth of the patient; after heat the cautery, for in this way it will form soon, and put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery cools down; do this often, because the pain will be worse the next day or the day after.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter in the hurry of this cautery, and then he eats it quickly; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a cauterization with the hair of the head that you will want, and according to what you have power; and this is the form of the cane:
des scrophules	of scrofula
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofula is of cold moisture and does not obey the digestion by medicines, then heat the head cautery so that after it comes the form, and has II openings for the fumes to rise up at the cautery from the other side; and put the cautery hot on the abscess once, where it needs to be, until it comes to the root of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, put cautery according to the quantity of the abscess, and leave it thus III days; and put cotton wet with butter as far as the burning is done; after treat the hole with garlic and tar until he is well.
Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moisture prevails on the tonsils of the throat, and especially when it comes from a cold complexion, then the patient should be voided first by solvating medicines; afterwards he makes cauterization at the root of the throat, and you must not come up to the throat, and dare only a little taste.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards he makes another cauterization at the joint of the neck to the head of the spine, and let the cautery which is called "clave" so that we have the form in front of us; and cure the place as we have said before until it is healthy.
de la toust	of the toast
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all and the disease of the throat are due to cold moisture, and the patient has no fever or thirst, and the disease is old, then he makes ij cauterizations on the neck according to the form which we have said before; and another cauterization milks between the breasts; and let the cautery which is called  "clave" be made according to the shape that is in front.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see it, make a fire cautery by poking at all the spots called "pins" of which the shape is as described above in the ear disease; and the pins are up to 30 or so in number, with no more.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treating the wound according to what is described above for this ear disease, and the cauterization is done with three raies according to this form:
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And for those spots that are lighter in color, you should do three of them together.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After that, massage the patient on his back and sides; then lift up the collarbone with your right hand; and if the joint moves inside, then heat the fire cautery in two places according to this shape:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	and cauterize the wound until it reaches the rib, and the shape of the cauterization with the same cautery has four cauterizations; and because this is done with the cautery that has three edges, the nerves are cut according to the thinness of a thread, and the form of the cautery that has three edges.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	And never is applied on this nerve for there are eight cauterizations.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	After applying the powder on the cautery, grind it with salt; then let the patient rest, and do not move the limbs for a long time until they are well healed.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated from above, let this thing happen little by little; then make the cauterization with the thick cautery, or many cauterizations by piercing.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed from the bone and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When in the stomach come cold and moisture until he was taken out of his complexion, and are multiplied to him the catharsis, and the ways of cures accustomed and he does not benefit, then it comes that the patient is sovined on his back, and extends his legs and hands.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	Therefore after him do three cauterizes I burn the skin of the back per the quantity of two, all cauterize clavile, and two cauterizes defuers the two sides as much as the shape of the cauterizes is at three angles, and there is a part between the one and the other that they are not joined together when they go corruption; and be the cauterize so perfect that it blisters both parts, and the figure of the cauterizes according to this form without adjustment:
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if you see cauterize of a great cauterize in the stomach according to this form; and who has fear of this cauterize, cauterize by poking and signing on the stomach i. point according to the quantity that you saw in cheek; then the cauterize is at all the cauterize which is called "poins".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment for the disease that we have had before, as long as he is healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	Regarding the liver, when there is pain from cold and moisture and strong wind, as long as it is removed from its natural state by excesses; and the patient is treated for what we have said in the divisions, and he does not benefit from it if he is stubborn about his food; and the sign of three cauterizations according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, let go of the joints from which the cut comes; and leave a space between each cauterization the size of two fingers; and let the cauterization of the long neck of the torso, and do not press your hand too hard on all the cauterization; and let it be burned with moderate heat, and let the patient lie down on his back; and if he cannot, then let him stretch his legs, and raise his breasts; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	And if your will is, then cauterize these cauteries of the cuttlefish, if you are subtle and wise in the art, and beware that you do not burn all of it, for you would parch all of the body; and let it come no further than a pimple, for the cure is very subtle at this place, and the wisdom to see it.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is an abscess in the liver, and you can know if it is in the par or in the cloth: if it is in the par, then feel that the patient feels pain not too much; and if it is in the cloth, then feel great pain.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And then when this cure has ended the blisters, let the patient be silent on his head; and then sign with your finger where the abscess is, and then heat the cauterizer which looks like a raygun, for that is the form:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize I the cautery as long as the burn is hot, and come up to syphac, as long as the pus is all dried; after the cure according to the cure of the sores until he is well; and it does not need but this cautery use no fire that those who have studied medicine long time, and by which hands these diseases have corrupt any time.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Then he can begin to work, and I think it is better that it should be left alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	For the pleurisy cautery
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	For the pleurisy cautery The ancient ones said that one must make a cautery of the roots of aristo Logue, and in this way: Take a root of aristo Logue that is long, the longest you can find, dry it, and also make it as thick and as long as your two hands; and moisten it with oil, and hold it to the fire, and cauterize between the breastbone and the collarbone, and II small cauterys a little down in the part that is sore on the beard; and cauterize between the fifth rib and the sixth, by declining behind a little; and I cauterize under the breast, and I another one over the stomach, and I between the shoulders, and II make two cauterys back from the breast, the one between the shoulders. And do not press your hand, but open it widely as when you are smelling something.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And no elder said that any man uses fire cautery like a razor, and blows it and puts it between the ribs, until it comes to this aposteme; and he jumps for pain, as we have said in the aposteme of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work is fear or the patient dies now, or a fistula comes out that cannot be healed.
de la mice	of the mouse
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse from what we have said about the division of treatments, and it does not benefit, then they have three ways of fire cautery that are all good.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.
