Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way to sew up a wound so that you gather the solution together: or with needles, as we have said in sewing up the belly; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	For the lips, at home come inside the lips an abscess hard, resembling grains of sand, and small and large; then cover them with needles and tie them tightly in each part; then dip it in vitriol broth, until the wound is dry; and then let it air dry, and cure the place of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the cheeks
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a tooth comes loose from the gum, which the old call "albulus"; if it is necessary that you hold it with pliers, and cut it at its root, and let the blood flow or the air; then put on top of the root vitriol broth, or other restraining and drying powders; and if this tooth comes out again after the incision, and many times it happens, if you cut it a second time, and cauterize it: if it does not come back again after cauterization; and these are the forms of the instruments to plug.
des sordens	of sorrows
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	of sorrows
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary that when you treat the pain of the teeth you delay drawing them as much as you can, because there should be no excuse for not drawing them.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	So then, when the patient is forced to draw the tooth, you must be certain about the tooth that needs to be drawn.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Maitres times the pain of the patient left, and thought that it was in the tooth of Saint John, and made him pull the good tooth; and yet the pain does not go away because the evil is extracted, for we have already tried to do this to these elderly people; and when you are certain of the aching tooth, so that you scorch around the tooth at all i. a strong spatumil to protect the gums from all sides; then move it with your fingers or small pliers on the first and second hole and hole, until they are well loosened, then tighten the pliers firmly; and be the head of the patient in your good between your knees, and hold it well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After extracting the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not hurt, then take any of these instruments and put it inside each part slightly, and move it so as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is deeply lodged and broken, fill the space with gauze where it is stuck; and if it is carefully held in place with tweezers so that it does not break when you remove it; and it is necessary to thoroughly clean the gums around the tooth so that the tooth can be removed.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And do you well to take care not to break it and remain a part of it, and return to the patient by the evil of the root greater pains than the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And take care not to do so as does the ignorant doctor who, by his haste and boldness, often breaks any chariot and does not administer anything except what we have told you; but he brings about any great disease by the poison of that root or by the chariot which he breaks, so that sometimes the tooth is drawn by wine or ewe's milk and whey; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the tools, so that the teeth do not move at all when you pull the string, and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of thick limbs so that they do not bend at all when you pull it, and be made of good iron, and be toothed so that it can hold fast.
de la racine des dens	of the roots of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root is still when you pull it, then you must put cotton moistened with oil on the joint or with butter every day.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	as long as the joints are soft, for then the pliers that are called 'algefri' will not hold, and the head seems like a nag; and be inside made as a file and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots will not come out with all these pliers, then you must peel off the kerchief completely around the root, and put the instrument that is called 'altheri', that is to say, an awl, this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be large and strong so that it does not break, and the root jumps out by this, is good; if not, if you help yourself with all the instruments, from which the shapes come here after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps oneself with this instrument that has two rays, from which comes the shape here:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are before in the rasion of dens, and this instrument that seems a pair of great pliers, from which is the form here:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and this instrument is out that it cannot break, and know that many tools of dens are; and also other tools, which are not mentioned; and the master subtil trueveth himself by his own instrument, according to what his work and the disease show him, for there are different diseases in which the old man does not teach an instrument for the diversity of them; and if he does not break the cart or other bones where it lies, if he seeks the instruments that suit him, I have told you, and helps himself with gestures, from which is the form here:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And are big and well-fitting to hold the bone, so that it does not escape but can be held and removed; and then return him to his place with medicines suitable for this one, and if there is putrefaction in the bone, and it is small, then he puts all this instrument.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth do not seem to fit naturally in the mouth, and their form is ugly, and most especially in young women, it is necessary that you know whether the root is also in front of the tooth, and is not in its correct place, and cannot be sewn or filed: then cut it off; and if it is attached to the tooth, take this instrument whose shape we have described, which resembles a small pick, and is made of iron;
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cap fits and fits hard by the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that it can be filed, then file it with a file of this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is also like the lime that one makes needles; and in the same way the tooth bites and bites gently with the hands every day so that it does not move until it chatters; then the plane at the end to any rasier, and its edge is too sharp and bleeds the tongue, so it is necessary to sharpen the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not bleed the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth loosens
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth are loosening, either by percussion or by chewing, and the patient cannot press on what he chews until he spits it out, and you have cured them with restrictive medicines, and that doesn't work; then you should restrain them with a gold thread, because silver wire becomes green and rotten, but gold wire never moves; and let the thread be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you notice any decay, take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then place the bridges between the decayed teeth, whether there is one or more, until you have cleaned them thoroughly on the other side; then restart the covering up to the part where you started, and tighten your hand slightly and thoroughly so that it doesn't move at all; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it can't escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then tie the hair to a pair of pliers, and join them together, and pull between the healthy teeth, and place it so that it does not hurt the tongue; and then leave it so tight as it can endure, and if it falls off or the hairs run, hold it with another pair of pliers; if it lasts and serves for all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the trimming of the healthy two teeth, and the two bad ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	Then when the tooth loosens, if one puts it back in its place over and over again, as we have said; and no one who is not wise and patient should meddle with it, and never make the shape of a tooth of ivory, and put it back in its place where it has fallen out, and hold it as we have said, and it lasts and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of copper the ring of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No one time is the ring which comes from the tongue or nature, that it must be thus: If by accident of a sore seam; And the ovraiges are such that you open the mouth of the sick person, and hold his head in your hand, and let the tongue; then take the large nerve of the tongue, as long as the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is pain or no, and it is a sudden wound from a sore, so you will squeeze the hook and take the large nerve; and guard that the cut does not become too perfect, for the artery which is behind. And when you have done this, lift the water of rose and thus, or cold water, then put behind the tongue a piece of linen; and dip it each night, so that the leech cannot be joined.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the blood rushes out, put vinegar on top of it; and if it does not stop, cauterize it with the slow fire, which is good for that; then treat it with other treatments until it is well.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see a red or black color or a hard skin, then the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, because it is cancer; and if it inclines towards blenchory, and there is moisture, then pour the vinegar, and make it with a thin spatula, and deliver it from one side to another; and if it comes out of your vein, put vinegar on top until it is dried up, and then return to your vein as long as you draw everything out; then lift up its skin like this and that, and treat it with other treatments until it is well.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	No time comes from within the throat called "godath", and they are properly called "amandres", and when you cure them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, be careful: if it is an abscess of small size and light color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	If it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron either for fear of blood loss; but let it rest until it is dead, and then you will remove it, or else it would break by itself; and if it is a white color, and the root is thin, then prepare the instrument to cover it, but first see if the abscess is hot and calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then make the patient sit in front of the sun, and let his teeth be in order, and he opens his mouth and puts his fingers between his teeth, and presses the tongue onto all the instrument, so that this is its form; and it should also be of silver or gold as fine as our knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And then press the tongue against all this instrument, and you will see the abscess, if take the scythe and put it in the almond, and bring up higher than you can; and bring any thing of the webs with it, then the cap on the instrument, from which comes the form, that seems a lot of forces; and yet the heads are corbe, and one place to another, and they are very sharp, and are made of iron where or of an engine:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, then the cap is with pliers, from which comes the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And be it trenchant on one side and not on the other; and when you have cap one of the almonds, then cap the other according to this same manner, and after the incision gargarize the patient with hot water, and with ease and quickly, and if blood comes out, gargarize the patient with cold water, or cooked pomegranate juice, or oak leaves, and similar things, until the wound is well; then cure him as long as he is well; and never let other abscesses come in the throat than the two almonds, if cap them all in this same way carefully.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I medicined a woman with an abscess that was lying within her throat, which is to say a small-sized abscess; and I had it very well closed up all the way around her throat so that she could not breathe through the passageway that was stopped up, and she could not eat or drink, and if she had delayed for another day or two she would have died.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so raised that it had been there for two days through the two passages where the abscess drained.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I quickly then put the needle into one of the two passages where the abscess drained, and pulled it through hard, and in a large quantity of blood; then refitted another one into the other passage where the abscess drained, and pressed her mouth shut and pressed her tongue; then I filled another one into the abscesses, and only let out a little bit of blood; and so the passageway in her throat was opened up again, and she began to drink water and wine again, and kept on cutting away at that abscess for a long time; and the abscesses closed back up again, and filled the space that I had left empty, until they got very big; then I sewed them up and cauterized them inside her throat: so it remained stopped up; and I departed from those parts, and only God knows what happened to her afterwards.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the pain comes from the eye, and it is severe and distant, then it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is a large, rounded pain, then it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is healed as we have said in the division, and the healing does not benefit, and you see that the upper tooth is pained, and it is thin, then you should chop it; and if it is round and assembled and not distant; and it is bloody or yellow-colored or black, then you should avoid the incision of it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger in the eye disease.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its blushing and distant, let the patient sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue on the instrument which we have mentioned above; then cut the onion in the eye, and peel it off, and chop it with two instruments which I have said in cutting the two mandibles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cover more than the excess that is beyond the natural term; for if you cover more, it hurts the voice and speech; and after incision, use what we said in the incision of the two breasts, and treat until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has a fear of covering; then you must use fire cauterization for the sensitive part.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the way of fire cautery is sharp water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should put his head in your hand, and then press the tongue to the instrument that we have said or fire cautery paste, and confound it with sharp water so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and in employing the shape of this instrument, from which comes this form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the head have a hairline or a thread to put the medicine on, as if it were a spoon, and put the instrument that we have said or fire cautery medicine on all the medicine on the edge; and let the patient lie on his side, so that saliva and mucus run from his mouth into the medicine, so that it does not go down the throat and cause blisters; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the edge, the quantity of half an hour, as long as you see it getting darker and the medicine's effects are coming out; and if you notice, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton with the medicine, and put the instrument on all the cotton in the bag, as long as the cotton is wet; and do this often, until the cautery is perfect, then let it dry, and wipe after three or four days or five. And if you need to refresh the fire cautery of the medicine, if it needs refreshing, and after the cautery rinse with cold water, and cure by gargling as long as it is healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than the incision, except for the cautery. If she is cured by fumigation according to this manner, take calamus and ysop and oreganum and rue and camomile and avronne and similar herbs, and put them all in a pot or some of them, and pour water thereon easily, and make it boil; and the pot must be very tightly covered with strong clay, and place the instrument over it according to this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And be of silver or gold, and let one of the shoulder-joints come out into the mouth of the sick person as long as the vapor rises up through the cane until the uvula is dead; then begin often, as long as the uvula dries up, and keep that you do not make this at the beginning of the coming of the abscess, for many things happen; and do not make this but at the decline of the abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	Et s'il n'y a pas cet instrument, prenez un chien et mettez-lui une croche de fer dans la bouche, afin que la bouche du malade n'ait pas trop chaud; car la croche de fer ne fait pas sortir la vapeur brûlante de la bouche, et c'est un bon remède ensemble salutaire.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Several times it hurts in the throat bone or spine of fish, or nothing at all; so it is necessary that you should take what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you can see movement in the thing; and what does not open up for you and is put back in the throat, it is necessary that you make him vomit in such a way that the meat is cooked in the stomach; perhaps he will regurgitate a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or an old crust of bread; and you attach the string to the sponge, and then you swallow it; and when it comes to the place, if it hurts, then draw strongly; and if it does not come out with the above, then take the instrument of plunging according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the tip so that it can enter the throat more easily and lift the tip higher up; and beware of touching the epiglottis, so that none of it comes to the back of the throat or pushes the bone in; and move it gently so that the patient does not cough it out, for if he coughs it out, he will move it gently or push it back; if it goes down, let him pull it all the way back up.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the fluid in the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Once the medicine has been used as I said in the division for the treatment of medicines; and when it does not benefit, then look in the sun to the throat of the patient, because you press the tongue to the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the fluid, let it run down all the way to the small hook, or tiny claws that are worth to him.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, take a shawl, and pour it down the throat of the patient, then pour or pour from the collar of the dog, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	If the patient is scalded with water every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a full goblet of cold water, and open the mouth, and pour it down as if to choke, and move it in his hand often; and if soon after he feels the water, then spit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if he does not spit as we have said, then smoke the patient with assafetida, using the instrument that I spoke of in the smoking of the wound; do this many times, for it will not make him gag.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the way of smoking as follows: you should squeeze the juice out of the charcoal and place it under a coverlet so that it covers the whole thing, and in that hole put the instrument; then pour your smoke, and the patient puts the top of the collar in his mouth, and closes his mouth, so that the smoke does not escape, but comes to the throat; and the throat will now start to burn, and if it does not, then begin the smoking again many times; and make the patient thirsty, and give him salty things to drink and nothing to drink but water; and then, by this government, what is right for him.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument is as though one had twisted snares bent for entering into the throat; and it resembles a beak, and has a roughness of lime, so that whoever takes hold of it cannot let go; and thus is its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the capiters of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Mouths of apparent abscesses are, according to what the memory comes here before one and the other in this book, and they differ in perforation and incision; and it is in two ways, the first of which is in its own semblance, and from that which it holds moist.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for the joints where they are at a corner.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscess in the head is different from that at the base, and the abscess in the cheek is different from that which comes in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if at abscesses one must not pierce, as long as the bowels are dead according to their course; and if at such that it is necessary to pierce when they are cured, and do not die according to their course, as in an abscess of delicate joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come from delicate joints, and one leaves them as long as they are pus-filled inside, there is a risk that the ligament and nerve of the joint may become corrupted, which causes contracture in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or if the abscess is in the principal limb, and you delay the perforation as long as it is dead, it will harm the principal limb; or if it is in the fundament, then you pierce it so that it does not die; and one must not pierce an abscess that has been cured without a complete digestion, lest that which is in the fundament be pus-filled inside, and come out as a fistula; and cannot heal completely.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	Et it is necessary that you know the time of piercing the abscess which is bloody according to the fulfillment, and this is when the pain is calm, and the departure of the fever, and the easing of the pain and rash, and the discussion and sharpening of the head of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the piercing where there is more ease for the abscess, and at the place where it opens; and let the piercing be long in the neck, and the abscess is in the hands or feet, or in joints and sides and arteries, and everywhere they are even, and there is no pleurisy.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, it is according to that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when the abscess is in a swollen place, if it seems to you that you should let the piercing remain until it is confirmed by complete digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	Car if you pierce him before this, if you draw out the blood from his veins, and it is full of dung; and by chance harden his lips and his palate.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if at any abscess that are pierced according to the length of the body, according to which the members have need.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you shall bring small abscesses, small punctures; and in great abscesses, great punctures, and many wounds according to the appearance of their greatness; and if at any such abscesses one should cover with a cloth, and bandage; when they are well healed as sheets, and are softened, so that they are made as it were a fabric: and if there are any that are torn in three angles, and if there are any that are to be covered like a mint leaf, as it were an abscess of horns; and if there are any that are to be cut into circles, and other cuts and shapes that are to be covered.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the hopes of the bow do not move at all with the exit of the arrow, for fear that the patient will die, and you will not notice it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	So avoid this medicine with great caution, and when you have pricked your abscess, if the wound is shallow, then bind it with linen or old cotton; and if it's a large abscess and there are many pustules, then let each one of them come together like a pouch so that they touch each other; and if you have cut into the abscess a piece of skin, and you have sewed it up, then fill it with wet cotton or wool from flax, bound it tightly for three days; then open it, and wrap the bone in poultice as long as it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if there is blood coming out from the wound, if you bring cold water quickly and easily, and wet the cloth, and put it on the wound running, many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the blood flowing from the wound persists, if you bring it cold water quickly and easily, and wet the cloth, and put it on the running wound many times. If this does not work, you shall bring the government and cure, and the powders that I have said to put in their places in this book, and if there is an arrow inside, and the base of the leus or the aposteme is nervous, you shall know that you should put on tents and cloth wet with wine and oil; and if it is gangrene, and the leus is fleshy, then you shall wet the cloth with water and oil, or with cold wine, for three days, as we have said; and then clean out the aposteme and dry it and cure it, as it should be, until he is healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is known everywhere in the treatment of abscesses: but I have told you how one should go about the treatment of abscesses, and here is the ointment.
des soros	abscesses
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When small abscesses come out, and are handled in such a way that they become threads, just as the jaw of a goat, and many have similarities.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fat and also ones where there is moisture as well, like poultry; and some that are hard and bony at the base, and there is no doubt that the artery does not cause obstruction.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the torso so that you test all the instrument called "intrusive", from which the form comes out afterwards, what it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, and then let it be pushed upwards with a long one.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	Et when the moisture is gone, if you do not let the hair that contains this moisture dry out, for it returns to its place when left alone; then dip a cotton ball in Egyptian oil, if there is any; otherwise, in water and wax, and apply the wound, and leave it until the next day; and he who has been delayed will be healed.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the cotton begins to dry again on the second day, and the ointment, as long as you know that it does not stay wet; then heal the wound with ointment suitable for the purpose, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds only a little pus, if the wound is healed according to this form, then you shall cut your hair, and peel it all over, and apply all your cure inside the coat where it is; and if the artery makes you contrary, do what I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do the same for the abscess if it is painful, and cut the hair and treat it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut the hair on the painful abscess and wet it, for it is lighter because there is less blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if there is no moisture in any of these abscesses or the head, and I found one of these abscesses as a large, hard, and bleached stone, which could not be broken; and had any been hit, it would also have caused a wound like a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses that come out of the head, these should be cut off at their most dependent part so that the bowels are emptied; and treated as necessary.
des scrophules	of the scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times there is an abscess in the neck, and they open the arteries, and they come from the angry, and never come to another place or to the heart, and they are rotten, and they are entangled with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And every scar is properly inside its rib, as the neck and the abscess of the head, as we have said; and the appearances of these scars are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are some that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	in those that you see of good disposition to the toque, and are similar in color to the color of the flesh, and do not move from any part and are not deep; so that you cut them from above, and you scorch each part, and the two lips of the mouth remain as they were, if you need it, as we have said in the abscess of the head; and little by little, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or the vein, and is not too thick or too deep, that the hand does not escape, and do not look forward too much, that you do not cut more than you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you open a vein or an artery and it does not allow you to work, then put vitriolic acid on it, or some powders that stop the flow of blood, and extract the wound; and leave it until the abscess is calmed down, and the wound is softened, and start rotting.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound has healed, if you return to your work, until you have finished it; then examine your index finger for any small scars, if they remain, cut them and wash them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scab, then it only needs that you cut this scab at its root, but let it hang by a strong double thread, and leave it like that without any harm; then bind the wound with cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, and then heal.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you have all the scrofula, it is necessary that you join together the two lips of the wound, and sew them now, so that there is no delay because of its great size.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	It is necessary that you heed to cover the root of it, and draw it forth strongly, and sew it as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulas that have excess, pierce them so that they die; and pierce them in the same way as that which has been said before, depending on it, then put on with care and similar things, so that they corrupt who are delayed by corruption; and when the wound is well washed, apply ointment of healing, often.
de squinance	of squint
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient ones spoke of the tailleure of the throat; but I never saw it done in our land, and it is the scriptural word of their speech.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have squint, it is necessary that the split of the throat which is called "epiglotte" be removed; and one should not seek help from anyone because all the veins and the poring of the patient are to those who have a hot abscess in the mouth or in the throat or in the two mandibles.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the patient is in the channel of the pore, it is necessary to cover the epiglotte to avoid the danger that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we want to split the epiglotte, that we do so with three circles or four small splits from one side to the other, between the two circles or with the quantity of the split of the syringe, not in the cartilage; and these are adaptable to the splitting of the epiglotte so that there is no obstacle, and the vessel is long enough for this.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	Et si le maître est effrayé, alors il doit étendre la peau de la gorge jusqu'à ce qu'elle atteigne la mâchoire ; puis, éviter les vaisseaux sanguins, s'il ne voit aucune chose, et ensuite appliquer le médicament, comme nous l'avons dit ; et cela est démontré par la section du flux sanguin de la mâchoire qui gicle à partir du trou percé, et par l'absence de voix ; et laisse la plaie ouverte une pièce.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the hour has passed when one is doubtful about strangulation, then join the two lips of the wound together, and all the flesh comes off the cartilage; then administer medications that cause gas to form, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albu casim says that one should not do this until the throat is completely blocked, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the failure causes one to lose their voice.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Adonques, cope on l'epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII. Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	And then, cut off the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe, and this will keep them from dying; and the elder man ordered that the wound be left open as long as the evil of the disease has not passed, and it has passed in III days or in IIII. And then he ordered to sew up the wound and heal it, until it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw. I saw that a young lady took a knife, and put it in her throat, and cut off part of her windpipe; and I was called to cure her, and I found her also dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found the blood that had issued from it; and I knew that it had not been cut in vain, but that it went right into the throat, and the life was going out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried, and sewed up the wound, and healed it until it was well; and there came to the damsel nothing but a red voice, and she returned to her own condition; so that I said that in the sewing of the epiglottis there had been no need to fear anything.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	is called "hernia of the throat", and is a great abscess in the color of a jasper, and is very common in women; and it is according to two manners: natural, and accidental; where there is no fault at all.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accident is according to two manners: which one is like fat us, and the other manner is like an abscess that comes from us of the artery; and there is fear, and it cannot be done to fire anyone but in the little one, and test and search everywhere the intruder: if you find it like this too, as the fat does not hurt us at all, if he copes, or even copes our hair, and checks it well, if there is any; and search well soon, and cure him as well as he deserves, until he is completely healed.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways to describe us, of which I will discuss all the similarities; and now it is appropriate for me to make the distinction between us and them.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that fever and chills persist until the sweating is over, and then the purging is complete; afterwards, rest the fever and the heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With us there is no fever or chill or pain, and the remedy is ready, which is according to the color of the skin, and begins also like a seed, and becomes large; and are according to their appearances, whether fat or moist, and much of a color as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to cure the patient, that you test and question first all the instruments which are called "entremissoire", according to what their shape will bring or the paste that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method for probing an abscess is that you squeeze as much moisture as you can find in the abscess, and then move your fingers little by little until you feel that the instrument has entered completely, then it should be done according to the size of the abscess; then remove the probe, and take care not to hurt yourself.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If there is a lot of moisture in the abscess, which color it has, then do as I said with the other abscesses; and if after the probe there is no moisture, know that it is fat, so do it crosswise, and take hold of it with pliers, and peel it gently from each side and pay attention to where it lies so that you pull it out healthy with the knot; and if you cannot pull it out healthy, then pull it off in pieces so that nothing stays there.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if there is no delay at all, it returns to us many times; and if there is only a little delay, and does not trouble you, employ the wound with some corrosive powdery water, and extract the wound, and put on things that calm the wound gently, and cure it with other cures until it is healed; and if we are in great pain, so count the two lips of the wound, and cure it with the one who causes it to swell.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein beats against or otherwise hurts you, so hurry and employ the place of vitriole broie, and let it be II or III days, until the wound is putrid, and rest the incision of blood; then return to that which was delayed by the knot.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Look here at the shapes of the instruments that are inserted, and they are of three ways: large, medium, and small; and there are three quarters that are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and they are also like the needles from which sorcerers are made, and they are of yellow bronze, or of iron, or of silver, and those that are yellow are more proven to make a loud noise to enclose the corbels of fistula; and they are of three ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the width of the apertures.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the horses are from many appearances, as you see here: great, medium, and small; and if to the horses that have two combs of three ways also; and if to the horses that have three combs and are also of three ways; and if to the horses that have two combs, and horse with one comb only, and are also of three ways; and all these are necessary in their places.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The shapes of the horses are from many appearances, as you see here: great, medium, and small; and if to the horses that have two combs of three ways also; and if to the horses that have three combs and are also of three ways; and if to the horses that have two combs, and horse with one comb only, and are also of three ways; and all these are necessary in their places.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and place it back at the site of the injury that heals with the combination of veins, arteries, and never according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never does the breast of certain men swell when they begin to rot, as if it were the breast of a woman; and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wishes to heal them must do so according to this form of the line: b. to g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then skin the fat and apply medicine to the wound, keeping it wet with tar that burns; then join together the two lips of the wound with sutures, and treat it until it is healed; and if it is not healed or if the incision has not been completed, so that the disease does not return, you must fill the wound with moistened cotton immersed in a corrosive tar; and leave it until the余 余 余 余 余 余 余 余
