des apostemes des asselles	of the heels
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	are caused by hard scrofulous nodules or blisters, and if there is only moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	So then those that contain moisture should be cut according to this shape, from line .b. up to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the bow in the abscess is empty, then pack it with dry cotton, and leave it for another day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with ointment as long as it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is like scrofula, then cut it as we have said in cutting scrofula, and if the wound makes a bow, then apply fire cautery as we have described before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured, and the skin above it is tight, then often comes an abscess, and all comes to a burst vein and an abscess; and if you feel it with your finger, you feel an extraction; and if it is for a vein, you should move away from it apparently; and this is madness to pack this abscess, and especially when it is in the heels and ankles and neck and mouth of others, and there are many.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary therefore to avoid the use of iron cure, and that which is at the shoulder also needs to be avoided, and in that which is swollen with an artery, make a cut on top of the skin from long; then perform the incision as one does, and separate the artery from the threads clearly, as much as it is uncovered; then insert a needle into it, and make it pierce up to the other side, and draw out the artery with two threads according to what I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries that are in temples; then untie the knot that is between the two bonds of an introducer until there is nothing left, and release the artery; then apply the cure that I have described, so that the thread chokes; then cure this one with ointment coming before this one, until it is healed; and if the artery is cut for the vein, it is necessary that you hold what you can of the artery to all the skin, then insert a needle from side to side, and let it have two threads, so that you pull it from the other side; then tie the artery as I told you, or tie one of the two parts to the two bonds of the thread; and if you doubt whether the thread has gone out, then put another needle on all the thread, from top to bottom of the skin, and draw out the threads in four threads; then cut off the artery until there is no excess, and also cut off the knot and leave what is tied; then put it on a wet towel soaked with wine and oil, and apply cures of tents and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of the nerves of the neck
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As well as coming from the artery and vein, they come from the nerves of the neck when they are injured, or due to too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And that which happens more often to the shoulder and arms and in all of their joints, and this is a painful aphorism, and its color seems like the color of the heart, and it is in many dispositions without pain; and when it is stretched out, if the patient feels pain, and is not completely hard throughout, but mutates well on all sides, and does not go forward or backward, nor up nor down, and the one who is in the joints does not come together with force: perhaps there will be contraction; and that which is at the top of the head or the forehead, it makes the skin stretch out.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the aphorism is small, if he has a nail, and cuts it at its root; and if it is large, if it hangs on the hook, and scorches it, then the bone and assembles the wound to the stitch, and cures it until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	The large bellies hanging down
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	There was once in the wombs and nowhere else in the body, and it is a disease that is called "fungus" by appearance, and it is the subtle root, and the big chied; and there are small ones and large ones; and I saw one man who had two or three bellies that were more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, and they were white, and had a small root, and they were torn open, and they ran with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I took them and found in one XVIII ounces weighing, and in the other VI Z., and the ovations in the incision so that you look at the patient is moist, and the color of the artel is white and moist and has a subtle root; so cope with the spatula wide, and be in your presence the fire cautery.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess, and I will come to treat the leprosy after this.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the wound is well
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes by cauterization of a wound or cut of syphilis, and it is on the belly and there are some boils, as it happened in other cuts, or of blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is in front, or of wind; and if it's because of the cut of the syphilis and the issue of the boil, then the color of the abscess looks like the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and opening of different issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it's because of the issue of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when you press it to its two sides so that it turns, and then returns, and perhaps it is locked, and enlarges much at the entrance of the bath, and by strong work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, then this is a light thing, and open well when you press it with your hand, do not constrain; and if it is due to blood, then open by these signs the large and hard absesses, and are fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to windiness, then it is hot at the base, and the opening is so that you observe that its appearance is due to the blood of the artery, or vein, or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is appropriate that you leave the cure.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you before, or chapistre the absesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if it is due to the bowel or bloat, then order the patient that he dyes his hair, and be extended all right, then sign all around the bloated; then order him to swell gently between your hands, then take all of the absesse up to all the large curve; then tie it firmly with a strong thread or rope, and let it hang; then operate on half of the absesse stretched out on the thread, and dip your index finger, and feel the bowel; if you find it caught on the thread, then release it, and dip the bowel at the far end of the abdomen; and if you find the bloat, then take it to the curve, and cut off the excess; and if the artery opposes you, or the vein, then go in, then return to your work and take two needles, and dip them in thread, and dip the two needles into what you have made a cross that you made pierce; then strain the absesse in four directions on the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the thread hanging as long as it putrefies, and cut off the bad part by itself; or you chop it when it is thin and putrid, then cure what needs to be cured, and cut off the absesse as we have said; and remove the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place from what is due, and weld the place.
dou chancre	dou Chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	dou Chancre
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the incisions, when they are in their place and you can remove them, as we have said, do so by purging the disease of black bile once; then make the patient well if he shows evident repletion, then afire the patient with good heat for incising; then pour your oncines or cancer, and hair all over, and break open the bone all over without leaving any; and let the blood run freely, and squeeze it hard at your hand or at anything, and if the blood flowings oppose the incision of the artery or vein, cauterize until the flux is staunched; then treat with other treatments until he is cured.
de ydropisie	from dropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	From dropsy
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And be cut from two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	a point, and be cut from two parts. On the skin, and let it hang down so that it dangles as much as possible when you put it on, and look whether the dropsy is directed towards the intestines: then you should cut upwards from the knuckle of the little finger; and if it is due to liver disease, you should cut at the left knuckle; and if it is due to fat, you should cut at the right, and let the weak liquid run out; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and pour it out, and hold your hand over all the spatumile between the skin and the sinew as much as one fingernail or more; then pierce the sinew until the spatumile comes to the level of the water, and then lift it up, and pour out this instrument where there is the form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Et est semblant à une caine d'argent subtil, et est d'airain ou d'archut léger, et a en la partie desoz i petit pertus; et ou coûté d'une part, III pertus; et II d'autre part, et I d'autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c'est li forme de l'incision dont li scribes taille la penne:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	And is like a silver-white cane, and is of brass or light copper, and has in the middle a small hole; and where it costs on one side, III holes; and II on another side, and I on another; and is the head cut so as to look like a pen, and this is the shape of the incision which the scribes cut the pen:
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the disease, and you leave it wet, whether the cure of the grave or sand is hot, and by sweating or bathing in water and in the sun, and if it becomes dark from drinking; and the cure of drying medicines as long as he is healthy, and cauterize on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after extraction of water, as I said above.
de l’estopement de la verge	For stopping the flow of semen
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	Do not give birth to a child who does not have an obstruction in the penis, or if the obstruction is small, or if it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If, at some point, he does not pierce the most delicate part of the sperm with this method:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then, put the narrow part of the penis, which is very delicate, according to this form: and tie it and hold it like that for three days or four; and when it begins to urinate, if the tip remains closed, let the urine flow, and then reset it; and perhaps it will not be noticed, because the urine that comes out strongly does not leave the tip closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	The tongue of which the hole is tight, if it is medicine with a drop of wine, as we have said, if it expands.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the hernia in its natural place are blighted, because no child is born with a hernia at the root of the penis, for it cannot urinate until it raises its penis; and cannot ejaculate unless the material can come out as far as the testicles, and this is a very bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the way to work on it is that the patient lies down flat on his back, then the root of the penis and the scrotum are like the size of a feather; so that the hernia pops in the middle, as it should; and you must guard against an escape of blood which often comes, and if it escapes, let the one who escapes bleed, and cure the wound until it is well.
des pustules de la verge	of the warts of the penis
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Several times a warts come in the penis, and has an ugly appearance; and there are evil and not evil; so you must squeeze them with a fine needle and clean them all, then put cotton wet in Egyptian ointment; then cure it with diafinicon as long as he is healthy.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the warts are evil, of purple color and depleting, you must bring fire cautery.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cleaned it, and if the warts are in the tip of the penis, and some part is inside the skin and another part outside, you must first remove the warts that are inside; and when they are sewn, then cure the outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat it together, if the head of the penis is not assured, it may be pierced, and comes blackness and corruption in his penis and where coion; so you must burn all that is black and corrupted, then put on plaster made of honey and flour which is made from apple tree bark and dates, and then cure with other cures as long as he is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if pain comes, then administer the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And if pain comes, then administer the lunar cautery according to this form: For exudation of blood, as when there is corruption; and if the foreskin is corrupted and withdrawn, then you should boil or cut with an iron knife a cord from the penis, and let the patient pee; and since, if it is a grief thing to speak of that, then you should scrape it with a spatumil any where on the head of the penis and the skin; then carefully separate them, and place a thin cloth of linen wet in cold water, so that it does not scar again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a continuous wound if it is like the other wounds; however, when we perform this work of our will and especially on children, it is necessary to do it in the best way and with the least effort for salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the old people did not mention circumcision of their children, because they do not use it in their law, and we only have this by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have heard the greatest part of the masters and the wise people who made circumcision between Y-d’Or and with force and for all kinds of things; so it was that he cut off the skin, and by chance if one cut on that, he delayed that one.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or it heals over again, and the pain is doubled, and the cleaning which comes from there is not certain at all; and by chance if one cuts on that, the nail also breaks, and the work is ruined, and often they are born like this so that there is no need for cleaning, and I have wanted it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	I have found the goodness of the experiment in the mouth-washing that is done at all times with such force; for the force cuts just as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, cut it evenly all around; but the thread should be well wrapped around the skin; and let the manner of the first work be such that you make the child think, if he hears, that you do not force the thread tightly around the peg so much, and then let it slide in all directions as you can; then let it rest between your hands straight, and turn the forces between your hands or toes so that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then bottle your hand to the peg and blow or suck, and turn it upwards so that the head of the peg is in place; then clean it well of the dirt that has gathered on it, then tie the thread tightly with a double knot, then tie one end to the other; and hold it between the two knots at the second knothole, and cut between the two threads, then lay the thread flat on top of the powder, then wrap the powder with glue made from cooked sheep's milk and good rosewater oil, and leave it there until the next day, and cure it with other remedies until it is well.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of force for washing is this: The two shoulders are soft and bendable, and the shoulder bones are also long and even.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of washing is when the needle slips during incisions; so you must stretch it out to your nail, so that the thread forms an abscess, and evenly, and if you cannot hold it in place with your finger, then hold it between pliers, and then cut it.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If it continues for three days, and that which is sore at the root of the penis is swollen, if he leaves it until the abscess has dried up and the scab has formed, and lightly scratches it; if you can move it thus, and keep away from the part near the root of the penis, it will not harm him.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Treat therefore the raw places of the body with powder, which we have spoken of in the treatment of powders, and if the application of the powder is too much, and it goes up, it will not harm; treat it then, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	dou retenement de l’urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retention of urine is due to a stone in the urinary tract, or frozen blood, or a bowel obstruction, or hay fever, or similar things which we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine does not pass, and you see that the retention is for the stone which is at the neck of the bladder, or at the top of the spine, it is necessary that the patient lie on his back; and let him be placed on his side with his feet raised above his head, and stretch out his torso on the side opposite from the spine, and restrain the patient so that he remains in this position as much as he can; and then it is necessary to hold the bladder at the top of the spine, by means of a tool called a “syringe”, whose shape is as follows: and let it be made of fine lightweight silver, like the feathers of a swallow; and let the tube be about one palm long and half a palm wide, and let it be thin at the top.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	Et the way of the issuing of the urine is that you take I double thread, and tie at the chief a piece of wool or of cotton, and bottle the chief with the thread within the syringe; and cover the superfluity of the wool and the bottle up to the chief of the syringe, then oint the syringe with oil or with butter and with a few drops of vinegar, and set the patient upon a chair, and raise the bladder and the penis with moist oil and with olive oil and with water; then put lightly the syringe within the penis until it comes to the root of the penis, then double the penis over towards the bottle; then bottle the syringe before jusc’to the bladder, and let the patient come up to the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order but that where you are leading him or she goes there bent; then take the thread completely all around the piece of wool and the piece of wool, and the urine follows the wool, then remove it forcefully, and make the urine run; and recommence the syringe as long as the bladder is empty, and keep the patient well.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When blisters or boils come to the bladder, and it is swollen, and you see it distilling water and medicines, then do this with all the instrument which is called "clepsydra", and that form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has III outlets: II from one part, and I from another, as you see; and let the hair grow by which the medicine drops so that it stops well in the root without addition, if one can draw out the moisture, and pour when the need is there; and when you see your medicines moving in the bladder, put the head of the cane in the moisture, and traing while you are doing so; if you draw out the moisture with the head, and then rebounce it strongly forward; if it will enter the moisture and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the form of the subtle clistere with which one makes the bladder clistere: it is here:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or bronze, and the head is above; and desos to the I heart or the ligamen knot; then take a bladder of sheep and put the moisture that you have seen to clisterize the bladder, then tie it between the II bladders formed of a good double thread, and heat that moisture on fire; then bottle the chief with the bladder, then strain your hand over the bladder towards all the moisture, until the patient feels that that moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, then take a piece of parchment, and make I circle, and pierce it roundly around; then bottle a thread in these openings, then assemble the circle as one assembles a dal, and put in it what you see of oil and moisture and water, and tie it on the instrument; and do so as you did with the bladder, pressing your hand until that moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already spoken about the ways of stone and extraction in general, and I have explained the difference between a stone that has been pushed out by its own power and those that have been pushed out with force; and as for the stone, I must tell you openly and briefly about its size. And as for the bladder and the penis, I will tell you openly and briefly about them.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone that is stuck in the bladder often occurs in children, and this is a sign that the water jumps out of the bladder, resembling water in its subtlety; and when it opens, it hurts the patient's penis, and it does so many times, and then it becomes smooth again; and the foundation is lost; and the recovery is lighter in children up to the age of four, and it is heavier in older people, and it is weaker between middle age and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, if it is appropriate first to purify the patient by enemas, to draw out all the feces that are in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never hinders to seek help from a doctor.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the legs and move them to dislodge them, so that the stone goes down to the bottom of the bladder, and does not remain in place; then make him sit with his hands between his legs, and his thighs apart, so that the bladder is all turned towards the bottom; then feel and touch inside; if you feel the stone in space, hurry now to cut on top of the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if she does not pee when touched all over, then moisten your index finger of your left hand with oil, if the patient is old and complete, and the bottle in its base, and feel for the stone, and if you feel it on your index, press on the neck of the bladder; then push from above with your index, and pour into its outlet, where you see the cutting.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder to his hand, and he commands that he extends to his right hand the testicles above, and with his left hand he holds the skin which is behind the testicles in the part where one makes the size; then he drinks the seed of copulation, for this is its form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make an incision between what is between the testicles and the foundation, not in the middle but near the side of the left hip; and let it be four inches long, and two inches deep, according to the quantity of stone, not too large; for fear that if you press there, which is at the foundation, it will cause pain without working; and know that there is a part of stone where it has angles and edges: such is easy to cut; and if it is round like a glans, its issue is lighter.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	A cell so that it has angles and edges, make the size larger; and if it does not bend, then it is necessary that you stretch it with pliers which are like a file on the head, to move the stone so that it does not escape; or you blow into an instrument which is sharp at the end attached to the head; and if you cannot engage it in this way, then it is necessary to open it slightly with a sharp tool, and if it is peeled off, then apply vitriolic acid; and if there are more than one stone, first blow the largest one onto the bladder neck, then cover it, then sharpen it, and the smaller ones after that if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	If it is very large, it is necessary to make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things come to the patient: either he dies, or his urine comes out by itself because the thread that holds it does not close; but anyway you push to extract it, or with pliers, piece by piece; and when you have finished your task, if you apply heat to the wound with incense and aloe and dragon's blood, and squeeze it, and put it on a wet cloth in oil and wine, or in oil and rose water and cold water, to calm the abscess; then remove the patient's tie completely by the third day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you remove it, if you raise it up with oil and water, then cure it with ash and basil, until it is well.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses come into the wound and corrosions, and congealed blood in the bladder, and be retained by it so that it is thrown out with urine in this or that way: then you must put your hand on the wound, and extract the blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder, and pour it out; then lift the wound with water and ash and rope, and aid it in all ways that you can, until it is well; and it is necessary that you bind both legs, and gather the medicines on the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it is down in the bladder, and stuck in, and the urine cannot come out; if you cure it as I have said above, that you cut many times, then excuse the cutting because of this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have proven this out.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take iron, forge it according to this form, and make it into three angles, welded together like a bar.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a file and polish the edge of the chisel against a stone so that it cannot come out of the hole; then insert the chisel into the stone lightly, until it comes to a stop; and then slowly turn the chisel in your hand towards the stone again and again until you can pierce the stone from the other side; and then soon after urine will flow; then press your hand onto what is stuck in the stone.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is quickly injured and jumps out with the urine, and the disease is gone; and if you cannot do this in any other way that hurts it, then file the edge of the stone and another on top, and make the chisel go between the two lines, and pull it out sharply, and then remove the line from above, and wash the frozen blood that is in the wound; and treat it until it is well.
de la piere des femmes	of women's stones
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	There is a chance that the stone is lodged in women and if there is no one time, this is a painful cure and is guarded by three things: one is that per adventure the woman is virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman well-informed who undresses herself to the mirth, even though she is married.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that one cannot find a woman well-informed in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that the stone in the woman is more perfectly formed than the stone in man, so that it requires deeper cutting, and there is much fear of it. And if necessity demands it, you should go to a midwife who is well-informed, and with very little she will come, and if you don't find her, do not seek her; but rather I cast her out of your city: then she should throw down her foot or foundation and want for the stone; and if she finds it, she should bind herself by oath that she shall cut off her foot or hand with the disease, and will and press her left hand on her bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she tears, so that it moves from the bladder's entrance to the anus, gradually until it reaches the root of the thigh; then chop on top of the bone at the root of the thigh against the middle where it is moved, and feel the bone in that part; and do not move your two above the bone or anus, and make a small cut; then pour oil into the wound, if you feel the bone so acutely towards the wound as long as the bone can come out, and know that there are many kinds of stones: that is to say, small and large, sharp and smooth, long and round, and which have rain.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the appearance, then know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if it doesn't go away, put vinegar on the spot, and keep it there for an hour until the wound is cleaned; then return to your work, as long as the stone is gone, and have the tools I told you about in drawing out the stone to help you with your task; and if it doesn't go away, and it's a artery that has been cut, put powder on the spot, drain the blood and lard, and don't repeat this, and leave the stone behind, and don't draw it out, unless by chance the sick person dies; then heal the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the fire has subsided and the blood is cool, and the leather is soft, if it returns to your work, as long as the stone is hard.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia causer
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	The water of the sea is not other than the gathering of white or salt water, which is separated from the egg by the skin, and is called "salt", and is never truly in the shell of the egg, if we believe that it is another egg; and this skin between the white salt water is what we have said; and this does not happen to be wrong.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the formation of this hernia is so weak that it comes out through the organs, and that material spreads out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And it never comes from beating on the organs, and this water has many colors: or it is color declining to yellow, or it is without red, or black, or white water, and so forth; and these are the signs of this gathering, for if it is white salt water as we have said, then the abscesses are round, a long figure like an egg, and do not open the organs, because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the own towel, then is the abscess with part of the egg, and because of this one thinks that it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the leather of the coions and the white syfac, then does it smell bad. So when you know the color of the moisture, then try on all the quire, from which its form is as before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the quire, judge who is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we cure it with iron, it is necessary that the patient be healthy according to his power and the repletion of his body; then let him sit on his back, on something a little high, and spread out for him some beds; then let him sit on his left side, and order the minister that he sit on his right, and extend the staff to one of the two ribs between the two coions; then take the spatumile rod, and wrap it around the leather of the coions among them until the end of the hand, and cut off the leather of the coions little by little according to the power; then pierce the white syfac with water at a large opening, and drain all the water, and then put on the scales, and close up the syfac upstream; and do not touch the keur of the coions, but only the syfac; wrap it all around or in pieces separately the coster of him carefully, for if you do not wrap it well, the water will return; and if the egg was too far from your work, let it go back to its place when you have finished working on the syfac; then assemble the two keurs of the coions with a seam, and then heal it like the other wounds until it is healthy.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you lay the eggs in doubt of the decay of blood; then take out the egg and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the egg is assembled in two parts together, knowing that they are two branches; then take out the other part as you did with the first, evenly, and clean the blood, and put on another wound with oil rosin; and put away another wool moistened with wine and oil, and put the two eggs, and put double sheets over them, and tie it all together according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two sheets, and fill them with wool swabs according to this form and join them together by stitching in the girdle of the braies, and let one of the shoulders rest on the foundation until the back, and the other at the arm part; and let the other two heads be joined together above the two arms, so that all is joined together by the restraint in the loop of the girdle; and is not medicined this ramice of cauterizing in heat of iron, but that you press the subtile cautery, and cut the skin of the eggs, and scorch it with this hot cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And pound the paste in all ways that you can, until it is finished; and be careful that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is safer; and guard against the evacuation of blood, and move that the work of the incision does not bother; and if anything makes you uncomfortable, or an abscess or an evacuation of blood or something else, cure what bothers you, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is fearful and does not want to wait for this treatment because of its horror, then introduce a perforation, as I have said, and it is that when you are sure with the meanings that we have said that ramices water is there, then make sit the patient on one raised seat; since then cut the abscess at the part that is sore all over, and put the perforation of the long neck through; and make the opening wide, so that all the water runs out; then put cotton on the place, and tie it, and leave it to run out the remaining water, then cure it as long as the wound heals; and if the white cloth does not let the water come out into the mouth of the wound, then you must put in it a feather or the instrument that collects the water from the drops, so that it forms as before; and open the wound slightly, and know that the water returns, and is gathered after VI months or so, and when it is gathered as before, then such will be the course of the patient's illness.

This is what I mean: with acidic superfluity that spreads to the testes, or by impact; and the color of the abscess depends on the color of the testicle; it does not cause pain, and it is a painful abscess; and sometimes there is an abscess that is painful and dangerous, and its color is dark, and it never comes from a vein, or from the swelling of a vein.

The dislocated shoulder, when treated with warmth and massaged, can be reset; however, if it is painful and difficult to move, it should be left alone for a while. Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	If the dislocation is located behind the shoulder, it should be carefully reset by a professional. The patient should avoid moving their arm and seek medical attention if pain or numbness persists.

de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscesses of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent. de hernie carnouse	of hernia cow-stomach

No time comes without a wound in the guts, as we have said, and open the channels; and do not release any of the intestines to the bowels, and if you do, it is little, and repair every hour; and nevertheless, if he stays too long in this place, if he thinks that the wound or the pus is there, as much as the intestines release; and what happens because of the extension of the pus that is in the guts, as we have said, for it is extended, then it softens and swell the channels and open them; and the cure is by cautery, as we have already said; and is never cured with iron in this way: but he should lie often on his back between your hands, then cut the place of the wound with a large needle according to the quantity of III days; and then extract the pus that is under the skin that covers it, and then take the thread and tie it on the visible place of the pus; and press it perfectly over the belly, then cut the two visible channels of the pus on the top of the thread, and cut them both; then remove the top of the thread, and do not cover the pus or stretch it with anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the intestine ramose; then cure it by the cure of wounds.

dou chastrement	dou cautere
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	For I know that this treatment is against our custom, and for this reason I would not like to speak of it in this book; and it is necessary only for two reasons: one is that the mare should answer when she is asked, and the other is that we have often had to use the treatment of certain animals to help us, such as rams and sheep and cats and others.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that treatment is done according to two ways: either by attraction or by a cut.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus. des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites

Hermaphrodite is according to two manners as men: one is that between the two testicles it opens up like the figure of nature of a woman, or it has hair, and sometimes in its scrotum there is urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and has on the loins like a penis and two testicles.

de la tentigene	of the tentacle
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	Is a joined one on the natural part, so much that it is too ugly to see; and some women have it also very much like a hand, and that is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you take off the surplus of the tentacle from your hand or oncines, and join it lightly; and do not cut it too much completely, lest there be an escape of blood, then cure it with another cure as long as it is sound; and with another joined one that comes out at the mouth of the mare, and employ it, and perhaps it jumps away, and is according to the appearance of a cow, and for this they called it the "old cow disease".

de erratique	of errant
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	If it is errant, so is the nature of the female who has not yet reached her time, or if the hernia is small; and is natured by birth, or accident through illness that has come about; or because she has been charitably carried, or with a subtle or bitter substance, and has been made perfect in marriage, or at cost, or delay, or whichever way it may be; and it prevents her from conceiving, giving birth, and perhaps growing flowers to bear; and the knowledge of this is through the use of medicine.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the hernia protrudes, it will soon appear, whether towards your breasts or towards the right or left.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle medicine, and it is close to the liver, if you hurry and turn it over: place your two fingers together, and let the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then form the two leeches, until the subtle medicine has run, and the hernia has been pulled; then take wool, and moisten it with oil, and put it on the spot, and let the woman lie on her side every day, so that he cannot stick.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the medicine is hard and thick, then you must cut it with the scalpel to make it look like grass.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the poultice is made of sheep's wool, then hang it on the arm and cut it; and add medicines that stop bleeding, such as those mentioned earlier, dragon's blood, incense, and a mixture of wine; then bring a large piece of linen cloth, so that the wound cannot close; and leave it there for a long time, and apply linseed oil; then treat with other remedies until it heals.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when the wound begins to heal, if you cover it in this way, then there is no risk of an abscess forming.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess that has formed in the wound should not be touched with fire.
des emorroides	hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Emorrhoids are openings of veins from which, without corticean custom, and when the emorrhoids are old they become thultul; and we have said in the division the appearances of horses, and the signs, and I will say here those who receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that the emorrhoids and the thultul, when they are completely formed in the womb, and do not appear on feeling, except for the cure by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the womb, one can feel them, are those who can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is therefore necessary that you put the woman in a cold house, then are the thultul to the nails, and the cope at its roots, then powder on restraining medicines blood, as it happened here and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then pour its feet against the wall for an hour, then put it in cold water; and if it comes to sanc, then let her sit in a decoction of pomegranate peels and oak galls and gall nuts and similar things, and then take barley flour, and confit it with honey and easily, and make a poultice with it on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops, that's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	And if not, then put vinegar on the back and do not hurt them; then take another one, and the juice of plantain or blackberry with old wine, and apply to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess is healed, treat the wound with oil until it is healthy; and what is called "balath" is red, and resembles sharp grass, so cover it as I have said in the book; and then treat it until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	the abscesses of the woman
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many kinds of abscesses come to the woman, such as syphilis, painful abscess, herpes, festering sores, fistulas, hemorrhoids, hot abscess, and many other diseases which I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.
