It is necessary therefore that I say in this treatise about the warm poultice that comes to the womb, which is not a warm poultice except for its heat; and if you know the work of iron, see how the poultices are heated at the beginning of their coming, and full of heat and fever, and if they become red you can see them.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	It is therefore necessary that I say in this treatise about the warm poultice that comes to the womb, which is not a warm poultice except for its heat; and if you know the work of iron, see how the poultices are heated at the beginning of their coming, and full of heat and fever, and if they become red you can see them. Do not therefore hurry to pierce it, but let it die as long as the pain is relieved; and then make it sit on II chairs, or II small chairs where it leans, and support its back and joins its feet to the side of the leg; and let its knees be spread out, and put its arms across its chest, and bind them well with a good bond; then suck his bole towards the left coast, and introduce the instrument with which one works the mouth of the womb, from which afterwards comes the form; and it is necessary that when you introduce this instrument, you stick the ring first to know the depth of the womb, so that what enters through the instrument does not come in more completely than it should, and does not hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the womb with cloth, so that the instrument does not harm it; and it is necessary that he put the cone of the instrument on top, and dip the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	Et when the abscess is opened and one pours liquid mold in the hand, if it is convenient to cover the head, let it be done with a sponge; and when the bowels are empty, if you put in the wound wet tents made of oil or green oil, place the tent completely over the wound and over the other side and dip the net in water or cooked berries; then the cure will come after two days of poulticing, until he is healed; and never raise the wound or the skin with hot water and honey, and then only with water or cooked roots and arnica. Then let him return to poulticing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound has healed over the bone, you must be careful not to cook it with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	of childbirth It is a craft for the Midwife to know the shape of natural childbirth, and signs if she sees the woman hurry down below, and desire to smell the air: so soon does the child come out; so you know that these childrens are according to the natural shape, and the issue comes from her head, and the second with him; and when you see these signs, then you should lightly press her belly, so that the child comes soon; for when it descents on her head, if he does the same with him, and is born clean by good purification; and what comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it comes never upon its feet, and comes from the chest or shoulders or the hands, or comes up her belly, or sometimes, and is turned around by chance at her neck, and in other evil shapes; so it is a craft for the midwife to be wise and subtle in these things, and to beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the shapes how she should help him.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If a man falls upon his head by natural fall, and the woman gives birth groaning, and the virtue of him is weak, if the fat he sits on a saddle, or women hold; and rises its nature of oil or fenugreek is cooked, and then poured the bath between his two little spatumile that here is the form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	If the second one is split, and he copulates with his thumb as much as the moisture that comes out runs away; and he holds his belly so that the baby falls, and if it does not fall, then it is necessary to use fenugreek musk with oil of sisament; then she makes her drink and shake off the condiment, and keeps her mouth and nose closed for an hour: then the baby is born.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	If the two hands go out again, it is necessary that you pull them lightly little by little; and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on a seat, and let her feet be up; then take off the seat from the ground, and wrap the woman, so that she does not fall when she stands up; and if her hands cannot enter, and the baby dies, then pull his hands with the knife that has been placed before, and pull out the child, and pull them equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the child's delivery between his feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes down between his feet, then it is necessary to raise him up; and then turn him over little by little until he is even; then squeeze his feet together and stretch them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	As soon as he starts to crawl, then instruct him to squeeze his feet together and make them shake a little bit; if he jumps, may God help him.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if he doesn't do it as we have said, then turn him over little by little until he is back in his natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then he becomes light again.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if he doesn' do it as we have said, then take muscillaige of the alders and oil of sesame, and gum melted, and grind them all up in a mortar; and put it on the woman's nature inside and out this ointment, then let her sit in warm water until she is wet all over, then make her sit on a chair, then make her shake and squeeze her mouth and nose, and lightly press her belly, because the child doesn't come yet.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	the birth of a child from its pelvis
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the baby comes in this form, so I put the ball in my hands little by little; then be tied to his neck, and hang down his feet, and lie on her bed; and fold her hands little by little, and then she takes them on her belly, and pulls the legs out, until she is completely removed; and if the baby does not come, so it takes its feet and moves its body, then moves its belly up, then puts your hands; and bring the baby little by little; and tell the woman to lean back as the baby comes.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	the issue of a child who comes with one hand extended
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	If the hand cannot be brought back, so the woman should get up and go; if she cannot go, so she should lie down on the bed, and bring her legs together; then I will bring the muscle-binder that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, so she should sit on a chair, then try to bring back the hand; and let the baby come according to its natural form, and make it twist, and tell her to lean back as the baby comes.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	De the birth of the child on her neck, and spread its hands, and his face turned towards the back of her mother's.
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	Now it is appropriate that the child's father hold him, then gently and slowly turn him; and when he is upright, as we have said, then command him to move his arms little by little; and when you have done this, put him in a chair, and command him to lean; and let her shake.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of this same manner to all the second
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes in this way at all the second time, so cover the second with your nail, as long as the moisture is empty; and if the child falls on its face and neck, so cover it with a blanket, so that it is not held, and dies the child; then put the child inside, as you have put it in the right way, and command the woman to lean no more: thus move her lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It is known that twins are born often, and never more than three or four at a time; and this is not an unusual thing, and does not happen often.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are an unusual thing, and do not live, if only one is born; but I know that, when they are multiplied, they are dislocated by the fire that devises them, which is bound to the boude; and they are never born naturally as all others, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	If they are born with pain, as we have said, and the gentle woman does it quickly and lightly; and let her do so as well as she can for salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Never are formed in the womb I or II or III or IIII or V or VI or VII or more up to XV, and they are all formed in the form of a child by the measurement of the wise glorious, and the midwives know everything about them, for sometimes similar things happen; so do as it is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman of a dead child or womb, as I have said in the division, and if it does not come out, and you are forced to use your hands; if it is necessary that you know that the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident by which she could die; if it is necessary that the woman be bent over her back, and her feet are raised, and her legs are inclined downward; and the minister bleaches her from both sides, or she is tied to the bed so that she cannot be treated for the delivery of the child; then rub her mouth with oil mixed with althaea and fenugrec and linseed seed, then wet her hands with these oils and these muslins; then pour them into her mouth lightly, then wants it to let it come out or he grabs it by its hair that is suitable for this, and takes care that the child is dressed properly so that it gives birth on top of it; if he sticks the hair in her hair, or in her neck, or in her mouth, or under her chin, or around her throat, or near her ribs, and the delivery is on the feet, if he grabs it or sticks it at coster's, and it comes out, it is necessary that he tie the hair to his right hand, and put the scarf between his two hands with his left hand, and pour it lightly with his whole hand, and stick the hair in any of these places that I have said, until it comes to the empty thing; and this is the shape of the hair.
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then take another one, or if you need it, so that the extractions are even; and then even them out by moving from one side to the other, so that they can come out, and hold the teeth of the onions so that they can hold, as this is their form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	and if one part stops, then apply some oil to its two sides and squeeze it in that part, and pull the other part; and if none of it stops, then put this onion or more up high, and do so until all of it comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	and if one hand comes before the other and cannot be brought back by the extraction, then you must wrap it in two sheets until it is all out; then tie it in the joint of the plant or at the neck, and likewise you must do with the other hand, and at the feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's loins are large and he is straining in delivery, or he has a sharp chief assembled there, then it is necessary that you pound the thorny spine between your two hands, and twist the chief and draw out the sharp one; or you rip it with the implement called an 'almidach', from which the form comes with the instruments or chaplet after this one; and so too naturally the child's loins become large, and then pull out the bones with nippers, and if the loins jump and are drawn by force, so they are split, until the moisture that is in the issue runs; and if it cannot come out, then chop it into pieces with a knife, and if it is swollen in the belly or beyond the sides, then it is necessary that you pierce it as long as the moisture runs.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if he is caught by his feet, then the pull is light, and his mouth to the mare's breast is light.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	If he is caught in the abdomen or breast, then you cover him with a drape wrapped around your hand; and cut the abdomen or breast until the moisture that is there comes out; and if another member has come off and stayed put, then press your hand firmly on the mare's breast and draw it towards her mouth; then bind it or tie it and pull it hard; and if her mouth is constricted by a fever that has come to her, she should not be troubled, but should be given moist and greasy things; and give her plasters, and chop in water that softens and moistens.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	If he is caught on his ribcage, and you can make it even, then administer what we have said regarding the living child; and if one has no power, then cut it into pieces, leaving none of the second.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, he shall bring forth what we have said in the chapter of the foot, which comes in the mare; and if blood comes from it, so be it restrained by water, and other remedies are brought.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb an embryo had been killed, then she consulted another one, and it was killed too.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, the wound in the foot began to putrefy, and it became very bad.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called in to treat it, and I thought for a long time, but I could not stop the wound from bleeding.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a strong poultice, and in a few days an bone came out, and after some more days another one.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled much, for this woman's womb had no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I wanted to examine the wound, and hand-held it while the woman sewed up the hole as well as she could; and waited a long time before tying this piece of cloth onto it; and I do not recall this chapter being mentioned until one day, when the master was examining an unusual thing, he knew how to provide help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the shoulder back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	This is followed by the description of the form of the press, how the muscles are attached; and at II turns become II shoulders of II lines.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the knots should be thinner than the strap; and made of ebony or box; and the mouth of the fist should be large, and the edge of the lips I must, and long a palm and half, and these two straps should be joined together by this same piece, which is folded in half on both sides, about a palm long.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Une autre forme, à sa ressemblance plus subtile et plus légère, soit faite de fuste d'ébène ou de buis, selon l'apparence des tenailles; et ait aux deux chaises deux ajoutsements, si com tu vois, d'une palme de long, et deux doigts de large; et quand tu vois ouvrir la marre à tout l'instrument, si fais s'asseoir la femme sur le lit, les pieds pendant et les jambes ouvertes, puis bouttes les deux ajoutsements ajoutés ensemble en la marre, et tiens le chef de l'instrument dosé entre ses cuisses; puis ouvres ta main à tout l'instrument, si com tu as fait aux tenailles égallement, selon la quantité que tu vois ouvrir la bouche de la marre, tant que le balais fasse ce qu'elle veuille.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is all mounted and multiplied for its appearance; and when you see them prepared, the faster they work, and the higher they are for their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If I do not trust you with the instrument, then you have not prepared it properly, for its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second is about to give birth, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to keep her head still, and then she should be made to spit out the child, and her hands should be held to her mouth and nose; and if she chokes because of this, it is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If that does not work, I can try to pry open the mouth with a toothpick or spoon, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the pregnant woman, such as mint, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or any of them, should be boiled in water or steeped in water on the fire; then put one end in a cup or toothpick from the pot, and the other end in the mouth of the woman, and hold it until the vapors come up inside the woman; then make her spit out, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If salt water is used.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	If it remains after this treatment, and is not cured, instruct the patient to soak his left hand in oil of sage or musk that has been left out in the air, then wrap it up, and then re-examine it; and when you find it, if you grip it and stretch it little by little correctly, so that the joints do not creak during extraction, but move it slightly to the right and left, and then twist; then it will come off and dislocate.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the patient's jaw is jammed, we have already spoken of the treatment for dislocation and the fumigation of herbs; and if it is only these that you have said, be careful not to mess up during extraction; but it is necessary that he who is at the jaw of the patient lies on his back in a woman's lap, then she clisters him with four-part oil; if she will and will let go, and will recover, but nevertheless, when she does so, if a bad odor comes to the stomach and head, and bleeds the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If one then needs to use smoke treatments that are appropriate for this: no one of the ancients has tried the smoke treatment with watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument to be used to smoke the woman during the retention of the first and second flowers, is this one:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is like the shape of a dog, and one sets the head carefully in position, and the shoulders wide above the fire; and let the smoke be over the coals, and the tan until it is spent, and start another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce through the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who have not yet had the foundation pierced, but a subtle surgeon should pierce it for him; and if one then needs to bathe so that he pierces it with his thumb, and does not touch it with any sharp object, and wraps it in a wet cloth made with wine and oil, and treats it with ointment until it is well.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not return, then put a lever under the buttock, and leave his hands free, and be ostenated when he goes to bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And there is no risk of sudden shock from a wound or abscess; if the former needs to be covered: if it needs to be treated, as we have said above, with the lever.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula at the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from the foundation are difficult to treat and grow larger than those that come from other places; and when the former is old, if it is opened, and then moistened with a slightly warm or sharp blade, these fistulas never stop; and they are caused by what comes out of the body or wind therefrom when the sick person has wind, and sometimes in salt water.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if they pierce to the bladder, and just to half of the penis; and they reach up to the intersection of the scrotum, and just above the navel of the cow.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And so you must know where the fistula passes to the foundation, and not where it passes: and that is that you stick your little finger or foundation, and stick a fine needle of brass or iron in the fistula when there is no curvature.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has curvature, if you stick a small piece of string or hair of a horse as far as you can feel the string or hair on your finger; and if you don't feel it, and there is no perforation, wind, or sight, as we have said: know that it does not pierce; otherwise, hasten to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula passes just to the bladder or just to the conduit of urine, if urine comes out, and cannot be controlled by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced just up to the joint of the uterus, so the effort comes up just up to its place; if there is no tortuosity and the invention of the painful inner part, then it is because he has bent it already, and there is no medicine or sudden relief by touching; and in these persistent fistulas there is no cure except work, and the vain dreams of the foolish people who get mixed up with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not persistent and is not old, there is hope of health by fire, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and he lowers his legs up to his hips, and his hips are bent towards his belly; then pour a bucket of water, or a plunger if there is tortuosity, until you know where the effort comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain in the foot, then he should insert his middle finger; at that moment he will feel that the nail is penetrating; and if you can feel between your thumb and the finger, then know that it is persistent; otherwise, it does not work because it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	If the patient feels pain in the foot, then he should insert his middle finger; at that moment he will feel that the nail is penetrating; and if you can feel between your thumb and the finger, then know that it is persistent; otherwise, it does not work because it cannot be healed. To successfully treat some of these, however, you must first heat the fine cautery according to the width of the fistula, as mentioned above; and pour it directly into the fistula until it stops hurting; do this twice or three times, until you feel that the made chars are burned, which look like a bird's feather; then the cure of moist ointment, while the char comes off, and then bind it with a bandage.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is healthy, then that is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If he is not healthy, then that cannot be good; and if he tries to pull it out, and does not pierce it all the way up to the base which is at the foundation, and there is a thick covering of cloth or drug between his two hands; and you see the fistula at that place where the covering has been pulled apart; if the cloth of the obstruction of the fistula is pulled together again before the covering, and then cauterized afterwards, as long as it comes to the top of the covering; and the covering will be removed, and he will heal; then put away those cloth covers that look like an owl's feather, and there should be none left.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the wound does not stop bleeding, and a cloth is put between you and the work, then cauterize it with fire or medicinal herb.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Car the fire cauterizes two bone things: that is to say, the burning of these joints and the searing of blood and the drying up of moisture; then he shall treat the wet tents with a mix of milk or cheese curds, as long as the bones are hot, and then burn the joints in the mixture; then cure the wound with dried medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	When it is restored, if it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes up to the very foundation of it, and is distant from the body, then cut off that part, and patch it up.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and there are two fabrics or joints or characters, or it is ready to pierce, then there is neither promise nor hope but by one of the three ways that we have said: either cauterize it as we have described, or cut off until the end, or if you can, place tents over it and cure it as we have said first; and do not go too deep, lest you cover the foundation, and let the excretion come out by the will of God; then cure it, as we have said; perhaps it will be healed; or you shall remove that covering and clean it up after it has been cut off from the end, or with a tent or another instrument pointed; then put on the dried medicine which is in the wound, as far as you can; then study to restore the wound, and hold back the fistula in the part beyond the foundation: so will it be lighter for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And there are no times of the tubercle according to this way: and when you plug the tent in the tubercle, and it is or it costit on the foundation of the leather above, if take a tent pierced at the top according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I plug it with a wire in II, and plug the tent at all the wire in the tubercle as long as it is at the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced in the margin of the foundation inside, then extract the wire from that is pierced, so that you plug your two at the foundation; and tie the head of the wire, and join the two shoulders together, and extract them one from the other, and leave them a day or two; and do not restrain it again, until the wire has caught those hairs that are between the two, and they chirp; then cure the wound as long as it is sewn and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, if you make it pierce with all your might, unless it is too completely sealed.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not right to make a wound by cutting if it is completely sealed, and then treat it, as we have said, until he is well.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spikelet that one makes the fistula with is sharp on one side and not on the other; and on the other hand it is not right to cover what one should not cover, as you see here:
des emorroydes	hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	 Hemorrhoids have two forms: they can be inside the fundament, like grains of resin, and small or large, and spread a little or a lot, and there is a little or more blood; and those that are outside are dry and tan-colored, and the cure for those who are inside the fundament is this: order the patient to strain himself to go to the chamber, as much as the fundament will allow, and let the fillet out; if you hurry and grasp it with your nails, then cut it off at its roots; and if it does not hold itself by its moisture, take it with a towel, or cotton, or a piece of cloth; and pull it out with your fingers, then cut it off, and powder it with hot powders that are for cauterizing; or cauterize it as we have said in the chapter of cauterization, so that other cures will not help it until it is well; and if the fundament cannot come out, then clisterize the patient with a hot and harsh clistering, so that it can come out easily; when the patient is clisterized, and the fillet has come out from the fundament, then the cure is easy; and this is how you grasp it with your nails or with pliers, and cut it off, then cure it as we have said, until it is well, and let him avoid being incised with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you prepare the suture according to this method: take a twisted thread and put it on a needle; then wind the thread over and under the needle, and pierce the needle from the other side, and bring the two ends of the thread back through the needle, and make them wide; then twist the thread into a form, then tie the thread, and remove the needle, and do the same with all the others, and leave it to bleed; then put on the foundation a damp cloth soaked in oil or resin, and put it on the foundation, and order the patient to rest; and then leave him until he stops bleeding, and when he has stopped, treat him with ointment and other treatment until he is well.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	to dry up at the end or base
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is drying up of the bowels in the intestine, and by nature, and when the disease is old and medicine is no good.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you resect the escrotum above the testicle, which does not allow it to be moistened; then treat it until it is firm as it should be; and if it cannot be made firm, begin to shave more vigorously than before, until it heals, and is scalded; then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	he vomited
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	It is a small appearance of decay before the chest, and it rot completely; and there is no need to cut it, and one can feel it like death vomits, and it comes in all the body, and more in the hands than in any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a feather from an goose, or a strong vulture's feather, and put that feather on the vomit until it turns purple all around; then turn your hand to all the feather as much as you can grasp all around the vomit, and make it firm, and scrape the vomit from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, do this of a dog's or horse's tooth according to this form, and be careful not to cut too deep and not to run over it.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	Do not let it pierce too deeply, for there is danger of causing pain and injury; cut with caution, and if you see, cauterize the wound as described in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	according to the form of the clister
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Do not make the clister out of silver or brass, or molten gold, nor out of small or great tools, according to the reason for which they are used.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	These are therefore small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the clister, small and great, is above wide, or the belly is tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and I have a hole or the belly is tied, as you see, and the chies are inside; and at one of the sides II holes are pierced, and in the other; and the belly is placed with a bladder of cow's milk or parchment, and pierced all around the small holes, and there is an interval of space between each hole, then pour into these holes a strong thread made of wool twisted together, and assemble the belly as if it were a cheese; and when the medicine is inside, let it rest against the instrument in front of a strong thread, then cauterize; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and grease the scalp with oil or linseed oil or something similar, then pour it lightly; then the minister spreads the medicine on his two hands until it is fully spread, then removes the clistere, and raises the patient's legs to the wall, and lets the medicine flow out, as much as it can; and if he sleeps a whole night, then that is greater help.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the foundation or abscess, so is the clitoris also very small like a child; and this is the form of the small clitoris under which the skin is drawn tight.
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken about the treatment of wounds in the section on dislocation; now we will tell you about the treatment of hands and medicines according to their condition.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are different according to what they are, and according to the places where they are made, and how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things that cause wounds are due to a stone's hit, a spear or a knife or an axe or a lance or a sledgehammer or similar objects; or they are due to the places of the body, such as a wound on the neck, or on the head, or on the back, or on the belly, or on the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you about the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with simple head wounds, because the memory [will come] in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, take care if it is from a movement of stone or of similar things, and the skin is all torn and the wound is large, and you doubt whether it is hot: if you do this soon, a healing will come to the head itself, if it is only blood from the wound, and let it heal in the opposite way from the part that was wounded; and take away the patient's eating of wine and fatty meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not heal, and its meat is made weak, and it does not drink wine, nor eat cheese; and put on the wound, if it is hot, wet with oil and anointment, or with wine that stings; and if it is not hot, put on it, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by the air, that I will speak a little later; and if he has moved it, put on some onions, until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is great as of a sword-tassel and similar, and the lips do not join by tensing, but are joined by sewing, as I will say to the wounds of the belly, from the stitch.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And if the wound is exposed to the bone and is small, and only holds for a little while, then cover it with skin; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of leather, and command the patient to eat large meats, such as roasted meat and similar foods.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find leather putrefaction, and it does not go down to the bone, then cover it completely and throw it away; then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be sealed with medicine, then cut the artery, and if that does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light; and that you put this powder in so that fire moves it.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the way of this powder is: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live coal three parts, and the powder finely, and apply to the wound, and bind it firmly, until it has healed well and joined together all its blood; and then bind it tightly, and leave it undisturbed, unless it swells, for we do not stop the medicine as long as it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never do we make this powder of coal alone, except when we have incense and dragon's blood, but that fire has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if fire has moved the wound, certainly it is wet, so put on this powder not at all; but put on some oil digested, or eggs of wheat flour made with water and honey, until it dries up; then heal it with other treatments until it is healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the fracture of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with subtle pincers; and I will tell you afterwards about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the neck wound
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	The wound comes from the back of the neck and is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but the neck where the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is on the back, then there is no other remedy than to let it heal, and not put anything restraining on it, for this hurts the healing and makes it retreat; and do not put anything on the wound, for the substance of the back is cold, and its connection with the skull, which is the highest bone; but be it sweet wine, as hot as possible, and mixed with oil of roses, and wash with water as well, and other stones of mineral according to this method, and moisten with oil.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then the bandage is tight and sore, then treat until he is well.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and he is sore and full of bowels, then cut or lower down; and if the artery is cut, and blood comes from it, so that he becomes dull and weak, and the cauterization has its work; and if the spitting in the throat is cut, or the tongue, and the conduct is preserved, because the meat goes well, if the taste on the chin of the throat is cut, and does not touch the throat but sets it according to its natural shape; and then he is brought forward, and left for some days, then he is treated with ointments that are thrown away until he is well; and if the wound has made an impression in the bone, then seek it; and if there are pieces of bone, then carry them out all hard, and those you cannot carry out, leave until the wound festers and the issue is forced; and if the wound is fresh, then powder on the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I said in my chapter on the plaster.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the lance or knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a lance or sword wound, and the wound is deep, then look to the wound to see if the wind has escaped the patient's body: because then the wound is deadly; and if it is not deep and is fresh all over the body, then put the powder on it at first, and do not tie it up so that it does not burst open, and let the patient lie down; but put ointment on it attractively, and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put raw wool in the wound to absorb the moisture, and let the patient lie down on the wound for three days, or three or more; then there will be no spasm, or bad convulsions from the heart's movements, or stranger things; and when you see the good signs, know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat the boils and other sores as long as they are healthy; and if they cannot heal, then cut open the area so that there is no more fistula, and treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	If the wound is from a sword or knife and it is deep, or has gone through the flesh, and if it is small, powder it, and if it has reached the bone, and has broken it into pieces, then cut the wound, and the strong ones will be tied; and if they are not tied, let them fester, so that the extractions may take place; and for other wounds on other limbs, there is a judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	Dou derrompement dou ventre
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the belly is great and small, and there is a great wound when the intestines break out, or when the intestines are torn from their place, which makes an opening for the wind; and the stitch is more painful, and there is no difference between the small and the great wound, because one does not put back the intestines as they come, else they will swell up so that they feel cold, and then put them back; and for the other wounds of the body and other limbs, there are three ways: the common stitches are made in the belly stitch and in the stitches of the other wounds of the body, and the private stitches are unique to the private wounds; and yet, all of these stitches are more private with the belly stitch, and I will tell each one apart and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and nothing from the intestine has come out, and there is something to be done, this is done in one of two ways: either because the wound is small, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen with cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is hot, warm it in the third way: moisten a sponge or I mol drapeil in lukewarm water only, or you cook in lukewarm squash and cypress and spike, and strain the intestine as much as the swelling comes out; and never do this with restraint, and let it rest that it may cool down.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling go away, if you moisten the intestine with water or warm it, and marjoram is cooked, because by this the entrance is closed to a small thing; and if it cannot enter, if you make a small cut in the wound with the instrument where you cut the hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to let it rest, that we do not cut it unless there is great necessity; and this is the instrument for splitting: if you cut inside the curve and turn it away, and see this form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the entrails are thrown out, if you can put it back in its natural place in its own proper place, for that is a mighty thing to do.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the belly, then it is right that you should make the patient lie on his back, and raise his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the lower part of the belly, then raise the head and the chest higher than the lower parts; and so it is right to treat what I have said about large wounds and painful ones.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, you should dress the patient, then put your hands between them, and with a wet cloth rub the whole hole from one end to the other; and so it is common to sew with needles, and it is that you should take a strong thread or more, according to the size of the wound, then leave a little space at the head of the wound, and stick a needle in it both ways, and make two stitches together, and put the needle through from one side to the other, leaving a little space between each stitch; this is how you should sew a small wound. But when sewing a large wound, you should take needles and threads according to the size of the wound, and pierce the skin with the needle on both sides, and make stitches together, and then put the needle through from one side to the other, leaving less space between each stitch; this is how you should sew a large wound. This way of sewing is most convenient for small wounds, because it takes fewer needles and threads than a single stitch; and it is that you should take two stitches together with a double thread, and pierce both ends of the skin together with one needle, leaving less space between each stitch; this is how you should sew when there are several wounds close together, in the same way as you would sew a sheet. And here is another way of sewing large wounds: take needles and strong threads according to the size of the wound, and pierce the skin with a needle on both sides, and make two stitches together, and then put the needle through from one side to the other; this is how you should sew when the wound is wide. And here is another way of sewing large wounds: take needles and strong threads according to the size of the wound, and pierce the skin with a needle on both sides, and make two stitches together, and then put the needle through from one side to the other; this is how you should sew when the wound is wide. This method of sewing is most suitable for large wounds, because it takes fewer needles and threads than single stitching; and it is that you should take two stitches together with a double thread, and pierce both ends of the skin together with one needle, leaving less space between each stitch; this is how you should sew when there are several wounds close together, in the same way as you would sew a sheet. And here is another way of sewing large wounds: take needles and strong threads according to the size of the wound, and pierce the skin with a needle on both sides, and make two stitches together, and then put the needle through from one side to the other; this is how you should sew when the wound is deep. And here is another way of sewing large wounds: take needles and strong threads according to the size of the wound, and pierce the skin with a needle on both sides, and make two stitches together, and then put the needle through from one side to the other; this is how you should sew when the wound is deep. This method of sewing is most suitable for deep wounds, because it takes fewer needles and threads than single stitching; and it is that you should take two stitches together with a double thread, and pierce both ends of the skin together with one needle, leaving less space between each stitch; this is how you should sew when there are several wounds close together, in the same way as you would sew a sheet. And here is another way of sewing large wounds: take needles and strong threads according to the size of the wound, and pierce the skin with a needle on both sides, and make two stitches together, and then put the needle through from one side to the other; this is how you should sew when there are several wounds close together.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought him the intestine, then he was eight and twenty hours old, and the wound was sewed up to fifteen days, and I treated it, and he was healed.
