Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfant, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtilitat, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	The vein is between the two nerves, so cut it long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The head of the cephalic vein should be tied, and the ends of the vein should be cut; and it is necessary to cauterize with fire from an olive or a laurel branch, for this is the safest way to treat a vein, because it does not involve cutting any nerves or arteries.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	All the same, it is necessary to desire the lighter life and not grieve for anything if it fails the first time, and one starts over again; and by chance, the weights increase in some men, when it fails the first time, but nothing grieves.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health is according to your thinking.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about the doctor, is that medicine should only be practiced to maintain health and prevent future illnesses; and it is done in one of the three veins: namely, the cerebral, the abdominal, and the basal. You must practice medicine at the beginning of a fast, in autumn or winter after eating, when the sign of fullness appears; and you must practice medicine on the first day or third day of the week, after two hours or three days of the week.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The doctor who is skilled in the diseases of old age does not have a set schedule but must work every day and at all times; and it is not appropriate for doctors to treat children until they are 12 or 13 years old, nor women who have been pregnant for more than four months until they have recovered.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Do not treat the elderly who are over 60 years old.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	If you are treating someone, in any way, it is necessary to fix the intestines of a light clister if there is a blockage, if it has retained mucus, so that the veins do not draw in the harmful waste that harms the main members; and it is not appropriate to treat those who are too bloated from meat, or drunkards, as long as it lasts, nor ydropics; and it is not appropriate to treat after a colic passion, vomiting, abdominal cramping, excessive childbearing, labor, staying up late, eating, drinking, or taking medicine if there is a chance it will help; then bath or wash, if nothing else helps to relieve the pain, and treat the vein at the navel, as we have said; and protect yourself from that day's work, and from fasting, lust, and similar things; and be moderate and restrained, and let the doctor who is treating you be higher than the one who is treating others, and rub his arms twice or three times, then pull the vein gently, because if it is too tight or too loose, it cannot stand; and then rub the doctor's hands with his left hand for a while, so that the veins swell and can be felt; then moisten the doctor's hands with the flame of a small piece of old oil, then put his right hand on that vein where he is going to treat, that the vein does not break and hurt him.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that run like strings to the worker, and if they have such ones that are plain with windiness, so that when one sets them on fire, if one takes away the flame, and cannot open the vein, then it is of those; and if he opens the vein, if it is too narrow, for this one it is necessary that the worker be on his guard concerning these things.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein is opened for the first time, it is good; but if not, then begin again a little little bit of that place where or on hospital, if the pains are not enlarged.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the pains are enlarged and the patient hopes, let him rest for one day or two, and do not tie his arm: perhaps there will come an abscess; do not enter or bathe, then begin the work again if it pleases you; and if the wound is small, or the cut is thin, and you doubt that it will not hurt as much as you see, then set fire to it all at once correctly; and work a little on hospital, so that the pains are enlarged; for this often happens, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see a vein inflamed, do not recommend the use of salt, and put a little oil on it, for it softens the heart of the blood and is wet in this place the oil that lies; and thus administer the oil to each vein that you treat the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and the same does three times and blows the air, when it is placed on the vein; but subtlety, it slips when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	If there is a large abscess, which often happens when the opening of the vein is small, then you must hurry and put a wet sponge in water and in silk a little hot, and hold it for an hour; and it is necessary that you do this after the blood comes out of the vein, and if it stays in place for a few days without any black or green color, then it does not harm him; and if you see it, put on any thing of aloe or mirrhe poultice made with juice of calamus, mastich, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there is an abscess and appearance to the injury of the basilica: so put your hand on, and if you find the soft place with the pressure of the hand, that is the appearance of evil.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid putting anything on it from what we have said, for by chance in the middle of the artery: but make him dry with plaster to harden the place, then heal it with another remedy until he is well.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat every injury according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the wound is black, let it bleed until it is red; and if you see pus, let it stand until it is thin; and if it is too warm, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And for those who are ill and need to extract the blood, make the wound larger and let the flames be broad; and for those who are weak, do the opposite, and heal them little by little, and let them not be cut in a straight line, but rather across, otherwise there will be a risk of blood loss and damage to the nerves, and it is better than the healing by cutting long.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for those whose course is in sickness, it is right to give moistened bread in grape juice; if he is heated, he will have a warm drink three or four times. And if he has a cold complexion, let him eat before the disease moistened bread in honey syrup, or in aromatic honey with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and beans, and fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he has a fever during sickness, after the exit of three or four pints of blood, it is right that he hums brewed wine, and fragrant syrup, and uses other things that we have said in the chapter or chaplet of syncope for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he vomits up any amount of food and then sickness at another time, it is right that when he is weakened by great sickness, he be healed little by little, according to the quantity of his continued virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who needs to vent his arms after the first sneeze, and he has a strong course, so that he heals 7 hours after the first sneeze or after the new hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who sneezes from another part, if he should sneeze in two days or three.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For he has a cough from the inner part of his chest, which causes fever; if so, draw out great quantity, and widen the opening as much as it chokes, then reward all the conditions for sneezing, and put your hand on his pulse when he sneezes, that death does not come in place of the choke, and this happens many times, when the sneeze is neglected; and it is not good when you dislodge his arm, and make him sneeze again with fire, and the opening is closed, that you press firmly on it; but if it is bent, let it extend his arm carefully, for that would be bad, but leave it until he sneezes a second time; or you touch it to the tip of the flame, as much as the mucus that is choked from the vein comes out, and put there a little string soaked in water, and press lightly on it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has burst, let it be and do not tighten it, as long as the abscess is subsiding.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires that the blood be drained a second time, then let it be done in the same place or in another vein or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein that goes into the arm is a second vein for the blood to go into, because it is composed of the vein of the chief.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the way of the wound is that the patient pours his hand in hot water, until the color is red; then let it move a little, so that the vein appears clearly, then wound now across, not large or long; and let the cuts be wide apart, and wound close to the joint of the hand, and don't pull out, if it's stuck, but let it come out easily; and if it's stuck in the wind, don't put the hand in hot water again, for we put it more into a hurry than into a rest; and the wound of this vein is saved more than all other veins, since there is neither an artery nor a nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The medicine of the right hand saves all diseases of the liver, and this is the method: pull out the hand, and dip it in hot water until the vein has gone, if you can see it; and then cut it off, and chop it up into small pieces, without grating it; and do not grind it too finely, for the nerves are all exposed and bare, and then put the hand back in hot water, so that it is not frozen in the wound, and cannot be drawn out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have finished treating the blood as much as is necessary, put oil and silk on it to hold it tightly together, and do this for each arm.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The medicine of the left hand saves the disease of the mouse, and do all the same as I have told you above for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The disease of the knee is worth all the illnesses that dislocate the body, such as the illness of the foot, and the stopping of flow, and the disease of the toes, and of the hips and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	The quality of this disease is that the patient should dip his foot in warm water and rub it on the leg until it swells, and tie it up at the joint of the foot; and the leg should be wrapped with rags, and more rags should be placed where there is more swelling, or at the ankle, which causes more pain.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you treat it on the foot, beware of the tendons that are dislocated, and treat it with the same treatment as you would a wound, and let the flame burn it.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if he cannot take it out, put the foot back in the water, and leave the swelling well drained.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if it needs to be sutured the first time, start again the second time a little higher up, because the blood is salty; do not doubt about the nerve, as we said, and in this way make the same shape on the other leg.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The blood vessels of the sciatic nerve are at the ankle, and the suturing is worth the pain of the thigh when it is for a wound.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of the suturing is that the patient gets wet or soaked, and it comes out of the ankle with 4 twists, because otherwise it doesn't open; and if it opens, then make it in all ways that you can, and cross it over; and worth more than you chop it, because the blood vessels are swollen, and it is very pulpy.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you don't tie it up, if the wound opens or closes from the foot to the little toe, and turns it over, and guards the nerve; and make the blood flow so that you can see it, and then loosen the bandage, and put cotton on it and hold it in place; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	vacuums
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	are made of horns, or bone, or glass; and the vacuuming is done in two ways: by striking and drawing out blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this vacuuming that is without striking... so is done with twelve points of the body: at the head, where the windpipe is; at the neck; in two places on either side of the neck; under the chin; over the shoulders; along the arms; along the legs; and along the ankles. And this vacuuming does not treat blood from minor veins that are scattered throughout the chest, or else it would weaken the whole body; but it should be done with fire or without fire in any illness that comes from overeating, until the whole body is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of illness it becomes necessary to ventose, or because of customs, we should regulate each hour in the beginning of the month or at the end and in each season; for there are such who, when they need to ventose, become very heavy; and those who experience a full face, and a swollen head, and a red complexion in their face, and in their head, and darkness in their eyes; and those who exhale a drop of blood from their mouth, and have escaped the tongue, and thirst for blood; and if there are those who dream, and see no nutrition, or nausea, or death, and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we saw these signs, and more so when the month is half over, we order them to ventose after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The surgeon's aid to the grief of the head... comes out through the eyes, and it is not until after the whole body has been evacuated that this ventilation takes place; and this ventilation is in place of the relief of the cerebral pain, and it is not suitable for those of a cold complexion, or those who are hoarse, because it does them great harm; and for this reason it is not suitable for those who stay up late at night, or who have had a cold recently.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are cured of it often become dizzy, and for this reason the suction cup should be placed a little farther downstream due to the doubt of dizziness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And the suctioning removes the wind from the throat at the level of the healing of the head and the bazileus, and for this reason it is used to extract it from the stomach, and to cut and fill; and it should be gently pushed back, because if it holds too firmly, it may cause dizziness or upset the stomach.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And the suctioning of the wind from the costels of the throat causes pain in the head, and blurring of vision and pounding, and strangles, and pain in the roots of the teeth, and is at the level of the healing of the bazileus; and you must instruct the healer that he press his hand to it, that he not cut the artery, and not let out the blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The wind-chills of the mouth bring on disease of the mouth, and decay of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and they are in the region of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The wind-chills of the shoulders bring on a disease that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The wind-chills of the arms bring on as much pain as three veins in the arms, since they draw blood from those large veins; and command the patient not to be too thoroughly covered, for their limbs are exposed, and there are nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The wind-chill that is on the back brings on hemorrhoids from the fundament, and similar diseases; and it is that the wind-chill be great, and of air, that it has the task of well milking; and perhaps, if it were subtle, it would break; and it would make great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The ventouse of the legs if they open wide, because they draw blood from all over the body, and match the old pains of rain, and of the womb, and of the bladder, and turn back the flowers; and are in place of the two shoulders, and of the two ankles, but they do weaken the body after a long use, and bring premature death to many types.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the ventouse is that you should first place it, and suck quickly, and put it firmly, and move it evenly, and do not cease doing this until you see the red and inflamed spot, and feel the pain of blood; then firm up, and remove the ventouses, and take care in the state of the bodies, for there are some who have great toughness, and clear pores: so it is necessary to wound once only, and to make deep wounds, and a little bit deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if it is thick outside, it needs to be pricked twice: once to soften the path for heavy blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if it is very thick outside, it needs to be pricked three times; and when we want to drain the blood little by little, we only have to squeeze once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want to drain blood, we start often; and if the outside is thick, we finish it completely so that the wound ends with a piercing cry, and because it comes to those who have hard and rough skin, and who have suffered much, you spread oil on the lees of the vials: if it is in summer, of violet oil, or of sweet almond oil, or of cucumber seed oil; and if it is in winter, of chervil oil, or of lime flowers, or of chamomile, or any other similar oil.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if it is a large and cold surplus, then take oil of amber, or of balm, or of anise, and the like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if a person has a sore that is tender and wide, you should not put oil on it, but you should wash it after the wind has passed with rosewater, or cold water, or water from mulberries, or cucumber water, or porcelain water, or other things.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have moisture, if it goes away with it, or with water from Myrrh, and Sumach, and the like.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large surplusages should rise with old wine, or with water from Sassafras, or with an infusion of fennel or chamomile, or other things; and it is not appropriate to saunter before a bath or in a bath, but after an hour or two; and one should not sleep after the wind has passed, and when he needs to be winded, as often as he needs to.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And beware of those who are ill with colic, and have too much gas and are inflamed; it is necessary that he eats cold things, such as pomegranates, endives, lettuce, and similar things; and he eats little, and rides a chariot, and wet meat.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion, drink syrup of honey and smelling wine, which is between old and new, and little food, and small birds and pigeons; and on the day that he sweats, he should drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men three times or musk before and after wind, to strengthen the members; and soften the skin, but it is not good for everyone; only those who are warm should drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The poultices that are not painful are those that are placed on the liver, and on the mouse, and podagr, and on the belly, and the boud, and the rains, and the hainche; because this member does not feel pain when it is put on the oozes, and we do so only in order to attract blood from one member to another, as when we place poultices on the nipples when the milk is not flowing; in order to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as when we place poultices on the belly and the boud in order to reduce the member; and so it is done when it is placed on the liver and the mouse when there is repressed wind, and these poultices are emptied empty because they suck so much; and they are never emptied together fire, and never plain water, as with pleurisy, and in this way we fill the poultice with hot water, or with water in which he has cooked herbs suitable for it.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup administered to fire is thus:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	The shape of the suction cup administered to fire is as follows: It should be two hands wide and half a palm deep, and it should have a small opening at its center, about the size of an awl, so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb; and in the middle a cross bar of iron or steel, so that a hand can grip it, and there are large and small ones depending on the illness and age of those who use them; for the suction cups of children are different from those of old people, and those of thin people are different from those of fat people.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And this is how the suction cup should be placed on the limb: Take the wax thread or bandage and place it across the center of the cup, so that the clarity is at the bottom of the cup so that it does not burn the patient; and then place it on the limb, and the two fingers should be on the opening that we have mentioned, so that when you lift it, if there is vapor, and then remove the suction cup; and take the bandage as before, and renew it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the vacuum pump therefore which is amineised in disease of pleurisy, there is no water, no verge nor perforation, and it is amineised only when it is plain of water, and put on the limb so little; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Do not amineize the sucks except in limbs where you cannot put vacuums because of their smallness, as lips and gums, and similar ones; and in the flesh of a horse, if it is two or three days old, and others like them; and the quality of using them is that when you find sucks that are in sweet water without risk of porridge, take them; put them into sweet water, until they are familiar, and have nothing in their bellies; and then let them be amineized from the vein and the vacuum, and then rub the limb until it is red, and put the sucks on; and when they are plain, and are cherring, if there is a place where you can put a vacuum, put it, because that is worth more afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then lift up the joint, and then with water, very well, and then squeeze it; and if the joint is too sore after the chest of the swallows, then moisten a linen draping in cold water, and put it on, until the swallows are dried out; and if the swallows are multiplied, then put crushed vitriol, or gall, and similar things on them, until they are dried out; or you put half of peeled beans on the joint, and leave them until they burn at the joint, now it will be stopped; and if you need more, take other swallows.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	If the swallows won't take hold, then rub the joint with fresh blood, or you put an needle in it as long as a swallow comes out, and then put them on, and soon as they feel the blood, they will burn; and when you see that they are peeing, then sprinkle a little powder of aloes and seer-sands, or ash, so they will pee now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This is the translation of the text:
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	The chapters of this treatise are many times necessary in the art of medicine, and serve for the restoration of broken bones and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Understand, you who read this, that the wise men of old did not pour this liquid onto themselves from any of the books or letters; and because of this, knowledge of it has been lost in our land, for I have never found a good one; and I do not know anything about it, except by means of the ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have practiced the science, and by experience, and through my own experience and custom. I have described in this chapter what is contained therein, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments used, as I did in the two chapters above.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore it is appropriate that we say in this book the sums of words and the chapters in which the sage places his understanding, and delays on truth, so that those who are tested may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d'une part et d'autre, s'aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n'est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c'est a savoir froides joutes, et char d'oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne mejunce nules grasses chars, et ne s'emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n'aies doute d'aposteme chaut, ne d'espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k'il a useit.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that the patient be fed with meat that is a great fattening, or viscous as cooked flour, and rice, and testicles, and pies of veal, and exercises, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For a great fattening prevents the break from healing more slowly and sooner.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of old and decrepit people cannot heal or harden the members together as nature requires because of the weakness of the bones, nor those that are too soft, like the bones of small children; but it is necessary to join them with large joints that stiffen and bind the member together, as much as they were before; and do not at all take away from their work, and for this it is necessary to feed them with great meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that the breakers are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break in the head is different from the break in the leg, or the foot, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of breaks.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that comes with age, and another from splitting, as the blade of a pen to write with.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it is a break with a wound, and a break is all a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each kind has its own tool for the restoration, according to what comes back to its place; and it is done by turning the bone by hand, and opening it well from one side, and applying pressure with the palm of the hand; and when there is no twisting or curvature, and the patient does not feel much pain, then there is no fracture; but it may have twisting, or a split, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not necessary for you to move him with your hand, but put on the medicine that comes next, and then restrain it now gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the break that went in the arvol, and are the II parts separated, it is now necessary to put them at a point even, so that the chaus come and i viegne; and if the chaus are hot, he leaves them no day, as long as the apostemes are calmed; then put them even at the mues that you can easily and safely, and know that the restoration of him is more easy than the restoration of the one where there are pieces; then restrain it, so as it is necessary here after.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are pieces broken, if the extension of II parts, it is hands or foot, or to your hand if it is a small member, or to II strings, or to a string and to your hand; and put the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are repaired, you keep by all means the additions in their places at the mues that you can, and guard that by your work does not come to the patient injury or pain; and adjust well the II bones of the member according to the best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And the test is good to the hand if it seems to you that it is not well: if the dressing is done well, and do not strain too much, do not press so as those who make it come by their overshot aposteme hot and contraction of the member, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is in order, let the patient chastise himself that he does not move it, neither awake nor sleep, nor turn, nor in any other way; and guard well that the member be so secure that it feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, he is not yet in order, and the disposition must be made that he feels no pain; and guard well that it be put rightly, that twistedness does not come when he is restored; and the quality of the member is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that the broken member is diverse in little and in great and in form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are little members, such as wrist and foot and similar; so wrap linens and soft cloth around them; and those that are large, such as thigh and leg: so wrap a wide and sturdy linen around, for the wide linen embraces the entire large member and holds it in place evenly on all sides so that there is no gap; then gently tighten, III turns or IIII according to the member, and hold back the hand a little at a time from the top of the break, then loosen the linen a little and a little, until you have pressed most of the blood out from the site of the break; then take another linen, and wrap it tightly around again; then go back to the broken end, and tighten it a little bit, not too tight nor too loose, as we said in the first line about; then place between the linings that are wrapped in linen or cloth, until they are all even, then tie them together well, if there is an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is an abscess or an inflammation, put warm things on it that are soothing, and let them rest for some days; then draw out with your fingers, and make a half-inch long notch in the middle of a wooden rod, or of a stalk, or of palm leaves, and make it according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	And if there is an abscess or inflammation, put warm things on it that are soothing, and let them rest for a few days; then draw out with your fingers, and make a half-inch long notch in the middle of a wooden rod, or stalk, or palm leaves, and make it according to this figure: but it is necessary that the stake that one puts on the fracture should be a little thicker and wider than the others; and also be as far away from the limb as it fits; then draw out on the stakes as you did in the first lieure, then tie a thread together, as in the first lieure on the fracture; the tighter it is, the better; and it is necessary that the thread be fine, not too thick or too thin, and made of linen; for if the thread is thick, such as I have seen made by the foolish ones who make their ligatures out of threads, it is a great mistake, because the lieure will not be even if it is too tight, and it only deserves to be tied so that there is less than two inches of space between each stake.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is pregnant and the teeth of the stars are cut after extraction in her health, then let them be bound with linen or another rag so that they do not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the bruise and the scar is broken, I will say the cure for this later on.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not come to extract stars from all the broken limbs the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it does not come to put stars on them before the fifth or seventh day, or more according to the severity of the abscess; and here is the way of the ancient emboweling to restore a break, a dislocation, and a twist: and that you take flour that stays on the walls of the mill, and confound it with good chalk, and put this composition, not too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of the emboweling restoring a break to many dispositions, and most especially to women and small children, for it is not too late nor too short.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plastering for healing fractures, dislocations, and twists: take resin and myrrh and ochre and asafetida and arabic gum and mugwort, 5 Z.; frankincense and aloe, 5 V.; alchemiş, 7 VIII.; and make a powder, and mix it with egg yolk of hen; if the complexion of the body is warm, then use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and quickly heals broken bones, and is useful for many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plastering for healing twists: take mugwort and castor oil, 5 Z.; frankincense and aloe, 7 VIII.; acacia, 6 Z.; Armenian bole, 10 Z., and finely grind it, and mix it with egg yolk or hen's egg white, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to make plaster for joints and bones that have come out of place, to soothe the pain, and to fix the size, use a fresh cow's skin, and soak it in water and oil, and put it on the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Cists emplastres ne restourent mie, mais il est bons pour apaisier d'aposteme chaute, et ostre proprement les dolors.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of applying an ointment that heals broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earth-paowl leaves, grind them together, and make an ointment.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of applying an ointment to heal broken bones and to soothe the remaining pain of an abscess: take dried fig leaves and earth-paowl leaves, grind them together, and make an ointment.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take roots of marsh-mallow, chamomile, violet flowers, wheat flour, and from each one a part; grind them together, and confer with wine, and the members are heated, confer with water or salt, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of applying an ointment that is stronger than the first one, in case of persistent abscess before healing the broken member: take roots of marsh-mallow, chamomile, violet flowers, wheat flour, and from each one a part; grind them together, confer with wine, then apply with water or salt.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of wormwood, and seedling of flax, burdock, melilote, and stinging nettle, and flowers of violets and chamomile, each one part with another; and grind, and mix with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the member, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Iocris in his book said that one should not put on the broken member any cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and said that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to me that one should put on the broken member, in order to restore it, dry things a little warm, such as mirr, aloe, incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way of making plasters which is good for wounds and pain: take wool and hair of sheep, or feathers of birds, and wormwood, and hemp evenly, and grind them, and make them into a plaster and put it on the flesh.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen it a little after, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor has his bone moved out of place; if pain comes to the spot, or itchiness, or no rest or swelling, so hurry up, and loosen it, and apply the plaster now; and take a light cloth, and a sponge moist with sea water, and dip into the water, and lift up the joint, until the itchiness ceases, and the pain is relieved; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on another dry cloth, wet with water or oil and tie it to a nut, until you are sure that the abscess is warm; and relieve the inflammation of the member, and alleviate the pain, then restart the gentle loosening, and a little of the plaster, and do not pull it as hard as before; and gently until he is well.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and painful and swollen all over, and you need to use plaster and binding, if it starts again, just as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the member at all of what we have said, but only after III days or IV or V or VII; and never more than XX days, according to what is seen, until the break becomes sharp, and approaches the shoulder joint; then restrain it more than at first, and let it fatten its flesh, as I said before; and if you see that the place is drying up more than it should, then dip it every time you release it in warm water, each time for three days, and leave it a little wet. By this work, therefore, cut off the nerves to the member, and carefully remove what they form, that restores the member incorrectly: this is painful, and if it is painful, and I do not see anything else but to make it limp and then set it straight properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the diverse ways of breaking.
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Of the diverse ways of breaking there are, and of various figures, the causes are different: for there is a breaking which is made by the impact of an axe, and all the bone is broken from its socket, so that it is like one or another; and because of this this way of breaking is called "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the axe breaks the bone from above, and this way of breaking is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two great or small breakings.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	Or if there is impact from within, or a crack, or a broken collarbone of stone, or falling on stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating break, which approaches to the skin which is out of its socket, or which is on the bone, and this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that has penetrated the bone as fine as a hair, and is a small fracture, and because of this it is called "capillaire"; and if the wound is made by a stone, or by a fall, or by some other thing, and makes a piece of bone enter; and if the head of the bone is placed so as to form a kind of ring as the blacksmith does when he works on the cauldron; then it goes into the stone.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often to those who have their heads wet, so that they are like a child's head; and to all these kinds of fractures, small pieces are broken off as if they were cards; and I will speak about it in due course.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all the kinds of fractures by traction on them, and by the tent of the tar which is on it; and by the corroding lead which is on it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair appearance is created by the fact that when the bone is uncovered and rubbed with fire, it opens the black fracture.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, be careful of accidents due to disease, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting, loss of understanding, extension, palmitation, feverish water, and hair standing on end, and other similar signs in multiple conditions, then he cannot recover by doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a hopeful accident, and you hope for salvation, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the birth comes first to you, and it is in winter, then you must remove the bone before the fourteenth day at most.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in spring, then you must hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue around the bone does not rot, and the accident we have mentioned occurs.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes just to the membrane that covers the skull, so it is necessary that you split the broken part in this way: and it is that you press the head of the patient strongly, and uncover the bone in all ways that you can, and on the shape of the wound more softly than you can, and if the evacuation of blood comes to uncover the bone, or an abscess, help him with what is necessary, and is that you fill the place of the membrane moistened with oil and rosin; and let the wound rest as long as the abscesses are calmed, and are certain about the evacuation of blood; then begin to split the bone, and this is done according to two ways: one way is that you split the narrow end in front, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then I bottle another way more wide than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have different kinds of tails, some are thick and others are thin, and they are pointed, and made of iron; and work lightly, so that you do not hurt the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and firm, it is necessary that you pierce it inside, so that you place the tails with barbs, not completely piercing through the bone's spine, and must have above the point a margin or a circle, so that it does not pass beyond the bone; and you need to have several, so that each comes in its place of the spine of the bone, so that you have barbs for all test; and this is the form of the three ways of bars:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality to pierce inside the bone is that you place the barb on the bone, and turn it with your two hands until you know that the bone has been pierced; then put the barb somewhere else a little after, and do this everywhere, and cut out the space of the bone which is between the pegs, and make it more finely than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you take the bone in your hand, or in any of the tools that you have, such as pliers, pincers; and keep from touching the cerebrum or the syfac.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced the bone and worked it, if it seems to you that you should take care of the marrow which is delayed in the bone by all the instruments resembling an incisors, but it is necessary that it be more flexible and finer than the other incisors; and if it does not delay any small bones or scales, if it is broken lightly on the instruments. Then cure the wound with tar and ointments that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way to work it is as Galen says, which is safer; and press it very hard, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you discover a part of the bone, where the break is open, so that when you have discovered this part, you put on top of it the end of this lens-shaped incisor, from which comes this form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and the part is wet in two sides, so that the cutting is opposite the bone; then hard with a small hammer above, so that you gently beat the bone all around, and you are well guarded from the cloth that is dislocated; if it is caught on the bone, gently beat the bone, for the bone does not cause great harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone break does not pierce until the cloth, and the bone is cut so little above, and there are small pieces, then cover again that roughness, and remove the scales with a fine razor whose you must have different quantities, to distribute in each case the most convenient, according to the work and the figure of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If there are more than a few sharp razors, and then some finer ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well done.
