En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other haircuts and fine shaves, you must bring about cause according to its adaptation; and this is a thing that is not readily answered to him who has put his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the syrup is uncovered, you should bring a linen towel, according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it with oil and place it on the wound; then take another towel, folded in two or three, and moisten it with wine and oil and place it over the first towel; and do so more lightly than you can, so that you do not weigh down the syrup, and then wrap it up again, and do not remove it except when it has dried on the wound; and leave it like this for a day or two, until the abscesses have become calm, then take off the wrap, and administer medicines as roots, flour of vitriol, powder of incense, and such-like things; and from these things make powder, and put it on the wound, and administer medicines without taste, so that the wound is kept clean, and do not allow the wound to remain unclean, nor do you allow anything to gather over it, because when bowstring gathers over the silk of the scalp, if it korrects and rots, it brings great misfortune to the patient; for when you put something bitter on the syrup, if you wrap it tightly.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, so that no bad accident comes to the patient, as we have said, if there is doubt without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blacken does not come but only because of the medicine that has been put on it, whose virtue it is, let you press one part of honey and three parts of oil and glues one garland, and lay it on his wound; then he cures in a way as he knows, until he is healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	You should know that no time are the two parts of the nose broken above, or one by itself, for they are two bones; and this bone is cartilaginous, and does not break unless it bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, let you drive your little finger or pin from the nose, and set the break even with your index finger, and at the opposite end, until the nose regains its natural shape; and do this lightly, and beware that the patient does not feel pain because of your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if his break is in the upper part of the neck, and cannot come to its place, you must put it even at the top of a thin ray.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if his break is in two parts, so deal with it otherwise, and hurry to restore the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or ninth, when the abscess has calmed down, then bandage the neck with linen strips, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind another with another part, if his break is; and may the strips be so thick that they fill the openings of the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And say that there must be no restoration unless the strips are moistened with tar and changed every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think that this is good, but it seems that the strips should be moistened with oil of olive and powder of mullein; then leave the bandage on until the bone is hard and the cartilage has healed.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And at no time put feathers in place of tents, and if it has a wooden frame, hold the frame steady, and let the wind blow through the tent, but do not make it so that the sick person can see outside.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess develops during surgery, apply a cotton ball soaked in oil or salve, or a patch of gauze.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess does not develop, apply an ointment of flour and incense, mixed with oil of almonds; then put it on light bandages, and do not bind the wound; and if the rupture of the wound is small, and it is broken into pieces, extract them with appropriate instruments, then cut off the torn part, and cure things that cause pain, and suddenly, as if it were an ointment and oil appropriate to it; and if there is no wound inside the wound, then cure the tent, and put tarpaulins, until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	About the rupture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken and there is no wound, and the break is so slight that it is not split into two pieces, but only bent inside, then it must be treated lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the break is on the right side of the jaw, you should stick your index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the break is on the left side of the jaw, stick your index finger of the left hand inside, gently pushing the break back into place, and with the right hand make it equal.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the jaw break is in two places, you should bring the two parts together, making them even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement from the inside, or the break, then stretch it out with a gold, silver, or silk thread; then put a cap on the broken jaw, and put a double cloth over it; and put a large, well-made piece of leather, the same length and width as the jaw, over the cloth, and tie it tightly to the mandible with a knot you can see; and order the patient to rest, and eat light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Et si tu vois que la figure change, si le désaisies au troisième jour, puis remet à point ce qui a changé; et met emplastres dessus, de la poudre de moulin avec abondance d'œuf ou de farine de sisement, après ce que tu as ôté le cerote; et met sur l'emplastre autre chose légère, et si l'emplastre s'agite, et la disposition du malade ne change pas, laisse-le tant qu'il soit sain; souvent il est sain en trois semaines.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if the abscesses break out, so that you send what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and a wound together, do not send a small piece of bone; if the wound is subtle, use instruments suitable for that.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is tight, so that you open it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have made all these bones, and there is no delay, if the wound is wide, put on it plaster that is suitable for this, to dry up, as long as it is well.
de la forcele	and with care
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	and with care Break several times in advance before the shoulder, and the break is according to three ways: or it is broken and torn into two, and there are pieces, and it is the lighter to restore; or there is a break with injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is as follows if the break is without injury, that you have two ministers, so that one dries up the shoulder joint; and the others extends the neck towards the injured part; then make the break even on both sides, so that the form is as it should be, and there is no appearance or haircut.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you have need to do more, so take a long round of cloth, or of other fabric, and make it big according to your need; and bind and tighten the roundness, and hold the roundness towards your hand, so that you make the break even, as is right.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot draw the head of the shoulder away from behind, so that it comes out whole, let the patient lie still on his back, and set the shoulder under an ear, and push the ministers of the shoulder down, until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then set the break on your two sides, and if you find it broken, so let you split it up; and draw the pieces lightly apart, and if the bone cannot join by any means, so put this instrument of the shoulder against it, to keep the medicine in.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and seems like a spoon, and is not a hair, and is also wide as it should be, according to the size of the bone and the ability of the work; and has two heads, if you see, and one is wide, and the other is small, as the cut made by you when you broke the bones; and when you are confident that the apotheosis is hot, if the wound is deep, and the cut is small, or if you doubt about the apotheosis being hot, then cover the wound with linen and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot apotheosis comes, if it moils in oil and honey and wine, and put on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	And if hot apotheosis comes, if it soaks in oil and honey and wine, and put on. The extraction of the bone, when there are wounds and no fracture, is that you put plaster on the bone with powder from the mill and ash of eggs, and apply light strokes, and put a spike around the joint, if you need to; then take a very thick band of about a palm wide, then put linen twice over the strokes, and plaster it on; then take a thin stake of three fingers wide and long, and wrap it tightly around that band, so that the top of the band is hanging; and put the stake on the break, and tie the band around the neck, and extract the joint slowly; and the release of each part, and when you see clearly that the stake does not move aside from the bone, then release it every day, and when the ligaments loosen, if they restrain; and make the sick person walk on his back, and put a little shift around the joint, to raise the shoulder; so that the fracture is lightened by the strength of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and do not release it unless there is no accident; until XX days; then start again with plaster if you see that it needs it, and extract it and leave it like that, until it is healed; and it is healed in about XXX days, and less for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	for the dislocation of the shoulder
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes forward, and there is no need to break the knee, if it is done so, and the bone, and do as we have said in breaking the forcelet of soothing an abscess quickly.
de la brisure dou pis	of the break from the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The leg is never broken in the middle, but it does happen sometimes; but it often breaks at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, if it declines to the knee, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of air, and sometimes vomits blood, and feels a good bit of pain in the broken bone, and smells bad.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lie down on his back, and put the cloth between the shoulders, then press the shoulders together, and join the ribs of the two ribs with your hands, and make it even as well as you can, in all ways, until the figure of the bone is like this; then wrap it in a bandage, and cover it with plaster, or other light material, and tie it tightly on the bone, so that it does not move; and return the cloth to its place, and tighten it, and loosen it every hour, and if it relaxes, tighten it again; and if it needs to be loosened for corrosion or itching that comes to the surface, or pain or abscess, do it quickly, and loosen it, and remove the plaster, and treat it with remedies; then remove the plaster, and tighten it until it is well.
de la brisure des costes	of the rupture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	I say that the rupture of the ribs does not come except in large ones after the back, and at the top inside, and do not bend much except because they are shiny; and the sense is good to the inquiry with the two.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And restore them so that you put the break even, as it is right.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then put on the plaster, and tie with a cord from an anchor, if you need to do so.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib break is declining inward, then the patient feels great pain and cramping, as if it were a cry; for the bone does not stretch the skin; and he goes blind, and constantly vomits much blood, and this is a grave injury to health, and they have put great effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if any of those who serve say that it is right to administer meat that swells the belly, so as to push the break out.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make this, unless heated abscesses come, if they do not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, and the health.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that we put cups on the place, to draw by suction from form, and it seems reasonable; nevertheless, there is doubt that the cup does not attract the excesses to the place for the disposition of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that one should cover the place with another wet cloth in oil, and put tents between the ribs to make the space equal, then cure it with the cure of plague, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain so that he cannot bear by the bone that pokes the cloth, there is doubt for the patient, so one should split above the place of the broken rib and put there some instrument to ward off disease; and then one should chop the bone, and draw lightly, and then sew the two edges of the wound, if it is large, and cure with poultices until he is well.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come up, put them on oil-soaked bandages and place them in the place they should be; while healing the place where it is to be an abscess, and sitting patiently on the coast where it should be until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the break of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No time comes with a break of the bone of the neck, and there is no need to weep; and also at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this has happened to anyone, and you can see whether he will be healed or not, if his hands become soft and swollen and dead, and cannot move them nor stretch them, and when you touch them with a needle, if he doesn't feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that he is mortal in many dispositions, and if he cannot move them and feels well when they are stretched out, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient is healed, if you put medicine on it.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	Et s'il y a une masse au dos, tu dois savoir s'il est sain ou non; si les os sont mous, et si l'accident qui l'a causé est encore dans ses mains, et s'il y a des ventitions et des evacuations sans volonté; et quand on le soulève sur son ventre, s'il y a des ventitions sans volonté.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And if there is a mass in the back, you must know whether it is healthy or not; if the bones are soft, and if the accident that caused it is still in its hands, and if there are ventitions and evacuations without will; and when it is raised on its back, if it can't.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is fatal: do not work in his cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come from him, this is the lightest thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you reward if there is an abscess, put oil or cow's milk on the spine, as long as it is relieved; then put on one of the plasters confortingly and drying, and tie it with a knot, and order the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that side where he feels pain, until he is healthy.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if some bones are separated, if it is necessary to put plaster over the joint; and set the bone, then join the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a stitch, then treat it with ointment carrying water until it is healed; and if the bone is broken, which is called "the break of the cheek", if you hold your cup in your left hand, and put plaster on it with your right hand, then make it even; and put the patch and tie it up; and if there are any bones that have been separated, then press them together, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	the break of the thigh
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	If the thigh bone is broken, and if it happens, let there be only a little reduction at the head; and let it be extended, and let it fall on the side, and let the pain and swelling come to the patient in that place, and do not cut off what is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the repair is that you extend your hand above it as long as you are on top of the break; and know what the break is and what its shape is; and if the break is at the root of the shoulder, then make this break equal, as long as it is in a natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or it declines inward, then make the patient sit on his stomach, as long as the repair of this break has been arranged for him.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it equal, then put on the plaster, and then put a board of wood or of board, and tighten the break so that it does not move, and hold the joint in place as long as it is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on his side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if the abscesses come out, don't scratch them, as long as these abscesses are calm, and put on what we have said before; and then return to the repair and tighten it as necessary, unless there is any bad accident; and this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	of the dislocation of the shoulder is what lies between the collar and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then one should restore it according to one of the two ways: one is that you take a strong rope, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And the two joints are tied together and hoisted up, and cut the patient on a bench; then, with an ax, split the arm over the fist, so that it comes to rest at the shoulder, and have a strong rope tied to it, and pull it down with all your might on one side or the other until it is back in place, and have a large beam of wood placed under it, then hang it from a heavy object or support it with your hands, so that the broken arm comes to rest as needed.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	The other way is that the patient is held by his hair, and the hand is tied to the collar, then you order the ministers: one holds what is above the break in his hands, and the others tie the whole thing together, extending each part as needed.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that extraction is too forceful, then hold the sinews apart, and over the break, and extend each of the ministers to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the break is near the shoulder blade, then you should put the sinews apart at the break, and over it, and extend each of the ministers to their part. And if the break is on one side of the neck, then you should put the sinew apart gently, without exerting much effort, as long as the break is even with the neck, and even with the ear; then set the break even, as it should be, and hold it in place, unless the arteries come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if the arteries come, then do not hold it back for more than seven days, and put a damp cloth on the break, and oil onto it, until the break has calmed down; then hold it in place, and the way to hold it in place is that you put the plaster on the break, then join the arm to the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or the side; and wrap a bandage around, and hold it on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its correct position, unless something prevents it from moving, or the bone is broken.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone doesn't move, then use a lever, and put on the fracture one more wide and strong than the others, and have between each of them two spaces, and let each be so big that it goes through the break three times; then lift up by the levers, as I said at the beginning about the paste on the fracture, stronger and less by moving away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the seat of the levers and the lifting up, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the member broken, and you doubt the abscess warm, let it rest tied for seven days, as we have said; then look at each three days to see if it is swollen or not coming to the member because it is too constricted.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If prescribed, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	If such an accident occurs, if only it were not that the shoulder is dislocated more than three days ago, and the patient sleeps on his back with his hands on his stomach; then put a cotton plug of equal thickness at each joint, and observe every hour during the day or night whether the figure of the limb does not move, or the ligaments are not relaxed; if it responds to the power of medicine, and give him food as we have described above, in such a way that the food is in the first layer. And when he begins to recover, let it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is usual that the shoulder and leg should be reset after forty days of all; and then it should be dislocated and administered baths and medications to set it right.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if it is stiff and encrusted, it will take one or two months to loosen it up.
de la brisure du bras	of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "foscile," one small and one large, with the small being at the top and the large below it; or perhaps the large one may break on its own, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small "foscile" is broken, the restoration is easy and the healing; and when the large one is broken, it is a bad healing, and more painful than when they are both broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small "foscile" is broken, then what you must do is to gently extend it and make it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	If only the large  "foscile" is broken, then you must pull it more strongly; and extend it on one knee, and turn the elbow of the arm with pain towards the ground, and the small elbow below the others, and let the patient cross his arms over himself, and a minister's arm at the injured part near his hand, or leg, and another minister's arm above it.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then make him hold it in place, according to his best shape.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is broken into pieces, place each one in its place, and if any of them fall out again so that they cannot be held in place, and you cannot restore them to their places, then do as we have said above:
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the break comes injury, I have spoken of it in the chapter on singуляр; take care.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of restoration come sore pustules, if I bind with a plaster made of rose oil and white wax that is neither too hard nor too soft; and I bind it carefully from above, until the sore pustules are calmed down.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then tie the oste with cerote, and I put the plaster of the powder from the mill with a lot of flour, because I put the splinters, and let the splinter be placed closer together than the others; and know that it must have VI splinters or more: whether the splinter is in one bone or II; and draw them up higher than elsewhere, and always less by moving away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter on singуляр; and may the cloth that is on the splinter be soft and moist, and may not be either too hard or too small, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And restore the limb and its joint after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if some bad accident comes to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, it is necessary that you soak the member in hot water until the itching subsides; and let the member rest without constricting it.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin again to extract, and if the joints are softened and the bone is displaced, and similar things, address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the healing does not progress with the member constricted, because it is too constricted, then you must soften it slightly and leave it for a few days, until the healing improves, and then extract it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said comes to the illness, then do not remove the member until XX days have passed.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	or en quenye, then the pent the hands to his neck, and be the necks equal, and se guard from movement and degradation, and sleep on his back; and know that this bruiser is restored in XXX days or XXXV, and by adventure in XX days, according to the compositions and complexions of virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the break of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	 know that at the back of the hand and to us two there are few breaks, and comes but that plied many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the plant of the hand is broken or plied, so that the patient dies crosswise, and sits correctly before him evenly; then put his hand on a cloth spread out, and extend the broken bones, and make them even miraculously, until they are well joined; and apply the plaster and stumps, if there come any, then put an ewer according to the quantity of the place; and let it be wrapped up in I draping of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if it breaks within the پاردرنس between the navel of the plant, then make a rope of drapels, and command the patient that he strangle it to his navel broken; and then take out of a long drapeil, and be its stake of keur so great as the plant of the hand, and strangle it, if it should.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if it breaks on the outside, then it is necessary that you put a stake on it, and another desoz in the plant, so that the hands are open and straight, then tie it completely around the hand, and stop the flow between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if it breaks on one of the two sides, let it be even, as it should be; and tie it with the plant, and if you see that it moves, put a straight little stake to lift the break, so that it does not move; and if the break is on the other two, as in the index or one of them, let it be even, and tie it with the sound hand that is after; or you bind them all together holding, so that they do not hurt, or put a stake on it, as if it were a pouche; and take care of the restoration and arrangement of the aphisteme, and help those who come, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the chest bruise
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The rib cage is often bruised, and it can be clearly seen when it moves forward and backward; and the healing process is as follows: bandage above the injury, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	The patient lies down and spreads his or her limbs evenly; then the injury is removed from the face, and both limbs are spread out equally; and it is when the rib is separated from the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the rib is next to the root of the chest, then one of the limbs is stretched forward at the elbow, and the other limb is stretched backward, away from the injury.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is next to the knee, then one of the limbs is stretched at the knee, and the other limb is stretched downward; and he places the bone back in its natural position with his two hands, and then puts the plaster on, and ties it up, so that it does not move.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess, let it be calmed then return to your work and your treatment; the time is made in some way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	And if there is an abscess, wrap it in a dry cloth twice or three times, and stay until the surplus goes away, then turn the leg so that the heel comes to the root of the birth, and put a long thread between the thigh and the leg, removing the kneecap, and bring the chief of the thread up; then turn again on the leg and the thigh the bandage, then put on the splint, and put a splint on the bone of the leg; then employ the space between the leg and the thigh with towels to make the strapping even, then begin to tie in three or four twists on the splint; and as you go up on the splint, and less strapping; then untie the two threads that you have put between the leg and the thigh, and lie III splints that are above, then return to the kneecap, until you come off the foot; and the strapping, if it does not move from its place, then let it be like this, then if there is no swelling or another appearance.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it comes out, if it dislocates, and addresses what comes out, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of the bone that hold on, if one can, yes; and if one cannot, then split the place, and pull it hard; and treat it as we have said, until it is healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the rectum broken as we put stakes there, as in the shoulder and arm; nevertheless, when restoration is made in this way, the patient does not cry out.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the rectum is restored in a day or less or more, depending on the differences of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the ganglion
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the ganglion there is little rupture, but it bleeds many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, if it is only a split or a gash, and has all the injuries, and there are no injuries, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the healing, if one puts equal that which is round on its two, as long as it can be assembled moved then put the plaster, and put a smooth stone, if you need it, and hold it in place as it should be, then make all the provisions that we have said in other breakers, as hot wound and another similar; put to each accident what is appropriate to him, until he is well.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the breaking of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called by right "mustelz" and the other "foscile"; and all the other breaks are the same as those of the arm, and for this reason the healing is the same as that of the arm, and all the work is done. And if the two bones are broken together, then the leg turns in every direction.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if his thin bone is broken, turn him around.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the thick bone is broken, one feels great pain and it can be seen clearly; and turn away.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Then apply traction, and make it even, and bind the bones evenly; but nevertheless, when a fracture is ugly, and there are many pieces, then the traction must be lighter and gentler; and align according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have finished your work, take two long hair braids that purple the leg on one side and the other, and are long from the ankle to the heel; then wrap them over it twice and tie in the middle, and at this ligature cannot go down to the right or left of the leg, and so is good; and if there is a hair missing, then put some in its place or another; and move each day the leg, so as to see if there is an abscess or any other accident; if the cure until it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	about the break of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but at the foot there is a fracture in one case out of many, and it has only been fractured in many situations.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	If there is a fracture in the foot, and you see these bones sticking out above each other, so that the patient can't put their foot on the ground, as if they wanted to walk, then now place your foot on two boards flat together, let the bones come up, then press them down until they get back to their places; then plaster it and bandage it, and place a small board under the stomach of the foot, then tighten it to the front of the foot, then you have wrapped blankets around, and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four have passed, if the swelling has gone down, because you will find the bones even, whether they are fractured or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	Et s'il i a aucuns des deux brisiez, si les restoure, si com nous avons dit as deux de la main; puis met au deux brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou deux, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j'ai dit, et l'estrain avenanment; et s'il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun deux une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu'il le teigne bien.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And remember not to forget the other things that I have said about other types of fractures; and attend to each injury as it deserves.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of breaking the bone with a sharp stick
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone is broken by a sharp stick, if the woman is seated enlarged, then she is inclined to the back part of the spine, and held from behind; then fill the vagina with cotton, and put in also much as it stands; then turn the woman over, and gently push the spine little by little, and then let the cotton fall, until it comes to the entrance of the vagina, and joins the bone with the spine; and when she urinates, if she holds the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back, and do this for seven days: so will be healed the break, and she will not die, take a bladder of cow's milk, and tie a string to the hernia, and pour all the milk into the vagina; then blow in the string forming, until the milk is inside: so will heal the break; then fill it with cotton, and leave it for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the hand or foot is broken, if it is restored as we have said with the bone of the thigh; and these fractures are not hidden from him who puts his study and work into it, and listens to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture means many things in the right way of restoration: listen therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the leg, when it is broken, take a duck's neck and pour the leg; then wrap it in linen, and leave it for three days or more, and it will be healed.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for him who has a fracture with a wound, even if it is great, such as the bone of the thigh or shoulder or similar, that he be healed now, so that the healed things which we have said bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, if the vitriol scald is not removed, then if you have nothing else, then start to restore the break in this same hour, or on that day, if the blisters are not coming out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the blisters are coming out, and if you leave the restoration until the next day, as long as the blisters are calmed down, and do not touch them nor on the third day nor on the fourth, for you would bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is appearing on the third day, it is necessary that you put it back with your hand, lightly and with small extensions.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions are not arranged to match your hands, then take this instrument made of iron, which has seven or eight inches in length, and its width is according to the quantity of the wound; and because it is necessary to dip it in water three or four times, according to what it is necessary for each break; and let it be round and a little thick, so that it does not press on the limb with your work, and is sharp at the front, and thick in the middle:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palanche", because the shoulder blade should be placed on top of the head of the bone; and it is bent once, until it comes back, and is even one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is small, and the instrument cannot take hold of the bone well, you must chop off the head of the bone until the instrument can have its way.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back together, as we have said, with an appropriate instrument, whether it is an incision or a saw, within your power; then remove that which is stuck in the bone with rough and small scrapings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone has been reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do so that it is in its natural position, then moisten the wound with black vinegar and properly sear it; and do not put on any linen or other oil where there is oil, lest it cause pus and corruption to come out; then administer honey when you have reset the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and wrap the covering all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not strained with the fracture; and many times this has been done to the patient, and brought out on him either death or corrosion, and the instrument has been made softer and gentler than for other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a good accident will not come, as we have said, and you feel pain in the place, then it does not convenie to put on splints; but wrap them tightly with hard drapes, and bind them fast.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days to bow at the wound, if you have put on what you have put on all alone, and apply an ointment that heals wounds, so as to heal the wound with an ointment of four-fold medicine and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it convenie that you dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and at night, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it convenie that the limbs be dislocated in such a way that the bow does not hurt them.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if every day passes, and he cannot put it back in place but it comes back to him bowing, knowing that there are small pieces of bone that have come off, so that you must tie the wound with tape, and all these pieces of bone that bring about pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula occurs or some other form of corruption, then you must treat it according to what the chapter above discussed.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken and opens onto the limb, as with the femur or shoulder blade, or other large bones, do not pull it out, for many times death results, but let it rot; perhaps after XX days or XXX, then treat the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, then let it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Of bruises that come from the surface of the skin
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Come often after the health of the break, especially when it's near a joint, and it is an ugly sight to behold the member's shape; and perhaps cannot make the member move naturally.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take heed, then, if we have broken ourselves: if we administer stinging medicines, as with aloe, incense, myrrh, and sarccolab, acacia, and others like them; or if we do not use any of these things, or all together, and mix them with wine that is stinging or with the oil of aloes or honey; and put them on the wound in piles, and bind them firmly, and do not remove the bandage for many days; and then remove it, and start again, as long as the nodule is ossified; or you may press it onto a well-made piece of plaster; for the quality of plaster is that it hardens all swelling on the limbs; and if the nodule has already become hardened like stone, it must be cut, taking care to remove only the excess; or take it to a barber, as long as it is hardened, and cure it as long as it remains sound.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the limb that is weak after confinement
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone has healed, and there remains weakness in the members that are small and delicate, this may happen for several reasons: because he was tied too tightly, and was not tied as he should have been; or because he had too many ties, and could not bring the member to its natural position; or because of numerous injuries; or because of too much movement at the wrong time; or because he has a lack of blood in his body, so he is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body soft, until the blood multiplies in him; and administer bath, and give pleasure and rest; then put wax on the member, so that the wax draws to it great nutrition, and rubs it often with warm water, until the nutrition corre to the member; and return it to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	two twisted limbs after sickness
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after recovery, and the bone is broken open, and the form of the limb is ugly, yet it does not harm its natural function: do not believe the foolish who say that the member should be broken anew at the first sign of pain, for many such fools have done this in our land; and these practices are blamed, and great harm and perhaps death result; nevertheless, if the nodules and torments are fresh, it is fitting that they be soaked in hot water, or that soft herbs be cooked, as foils of fat, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and the ointment made with a soft substance, as well-made dandelion, and you take the musk of fat, and confit it with the fat of wild boar or oil of sesame seeds, and make the ointment; or you take dried figs, and grind them with hay of corn, and similar medicines that soften the pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never let the neck be moved continually and longingly with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And so that there is no movement in the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if it is twisted and hardened, as in stone, then it must be opened with a sharp knife gently; and put on tar and study for the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations:
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, if it is now brought back gently.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if we delay, and the pains increase, and perhaps he re-sets him at his own place; for in this way, many times, pain and other ills are brought about; nevertheless, when this will come, so make the patient well, then let it rest, until the abscess is calmed down; then raise the member with hot water and oil, then gently adjust it, and cure every limb as the cure comes.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the ointments of dislocations of the shoulders until the foot.
des mandibules	the jawbones
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	And then, if the mandibles have dislocated, they are in two ways: either they are a little out of their places, and become a little soft; or they are completely dislocated, hanging down to the chest, and stopping the saliva from the mouth so that it cannot be kept shut, and wrap their tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, return it by means of several positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, you must immediately reset it, and do not wait; and in this way that the minister holds the chief of the sick, and squirts a little ointment from one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw within the mouth, the dislocation is of two parts; and the other two hands should be apart, to make it even; and order the patient that he soften his jaws, and move them in all directions.
