Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And let the wound be kept equal until it heals in its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And let it be brought back by gentle movement, especially if the two mandibles are together, and if raised with hot water and oil, gently; do not delay bringing it back, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they have been brought back equally, and the mouth of the patient is closed well with a soothing ointment made of oil and wax, then let it be gently laid on draping wet with the ointment, and sleep on his back, and let his shoulders be between two pillows so that he does not move or strive to turn over, but eat lightly, until the pains are gone, and the mandibles are healed; and then feed him lightly, and do not strive to open the mouth for eating or drinking, until the mandible is well healed.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be reset within an hour and do not return to their places, then fever and usual suddenness come, and perhaps a soluction of the belly, and perhaps vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see that, then you know that it is a sign of death; and many die within nine days.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	does not dislocate from the inside out in the continuation of the neck and the chest, and is dislocated at any time on the side, and it can be felt.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies on his back and extends his arms; then press the joint with your hand, and it will come back; then put the plaster and bandage on it and hold it in place; and the head that is turned toward the chest cannot be dislocated; if not, and if it is dislocated at any time, let him return to his place, as we have said; then put the plaster and bandage on it and hold it, and command the patient to rest until he is well; and thus is the shoulder head restored when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	which is dislocated only in three ways: either it has dislocated at the shoulder joint itself; or at the upper part of the blade; or possibly at the top, and never behind the shoulder, nor inside towards the neck; and many times dislocating at the blade's end, but for those who have a lot of money, because with them it would be necessary to go to the hospital; and for those who have enough money, let them stay in place, and return to place.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes there is a blow or a crack on some men, and the shoulder is dislocated with heat; and he thinks that it has dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Then you must test it, until you are sure of it; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And is known the dislocations when it goes down the neck, and sets a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find among them a manifest diversity; and you will find at the head of the shoulder a pit, and loosen the neck with the head of the shoulder, as if it were a fruit; and cannot the patient bring his hand to his neck, nor make any movements; and also, if it is dislocated upward, it is not hidden, because you see it clearly on the chest; and this way of dislocation is not only for bringing back when it is new, or when the patient has been imprisoned.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the way is that the ministers leave the patient's hand at the top, then put your sleeves off the shoulder, and bring the joint up by force to its place; and the ministers leave the hand, and extend it upward, because they bring it back; so come quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in our days later, it is necessary that the patient be bathed in hot water; and soft and soothing poultices are applied, as with an infusion of althaea and fenugreek and melilote in water, and are applied; then the patient is put to lie on his back, and a strap is taken from another shoulder of the same, not too loose or too tight, then the patient's foot is placed on the strap, and the head of the shoulder is gently raised, and the hand of the patient is pulled; and other ministers take the head of the patient, so that it does not move downward; this shoulder returns all at once, and you will see if you follow this way: and it is that you have a man who is greater than the patient; and he stands on one side of his chest, and takes the shoulder of the patient from behind, and lifts the shoulder, so that the patient hangs in the air; and other ministers take the hand of the patient and pull it downward toward his belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, then without anything heavy with him, the dislocation comes back now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And if the patient is too light, then without anything heavy with him, the dislocation comes back now. And let us also say that, and we stick a long brand in the ground, whose end is also like a pistol, and not too big or too small; then put on it the sick person, but so that there are drapes above, and the sick person is lying on the long brand; then extend his hand down from the other side forming, and the joint will return to its place safely; and if it does not come back by all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take a brand of II arms of great and IIII hands wide, which has the head on one side to enter completely into the assembly, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	And then he lays him on the long pole, that he might not wound the patient, and then he sets the shoulder of the patient; and he extends his arms over the long pole, and sets the shoulder upon the pole, and his arm at the top of the hand, and then puts his arm over a peg of an axe of length, and lets his hands fall, and leaves his body hanging on the other side: the joints are now reset.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, in any way, you must put a spear of wool equal, then put the plaster prepared with powder from the mill, with incense and amber, on all the shoulder and back; then remove the shoulder in advance, and tie the bandage to the plaster, and embrace the hand at the neck, and let the hands stay there.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he should drink little, so that the limbs are comfortable, for he will heal more quickly; and then drink a little more after five or seven days, and move them; and if they are hardened and not softened, they are healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is out of place due to moisture that has come or due to another cause, it is necessary that you apply cauterization to three parts, as it is placed in front or with the paste of the cauterization.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and he relaxes after seven days, and the joint does not stay in place, and he cannot raise his arm upwards, then you know that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is cut or stretched or softened; and you know that the joint has never been put back into its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the chest, and the nipples, or behind, is made by a blow, and an extension of the hands, and I apply another place; and treat until he is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes greasiness to the member, and slowly moves, so the patient bathes many times, until that greasiness is relieved, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	I know that the joint of the shoulder has been dislocated in many places, and in many ways; and if it is dislocated from all sides, most especially in front and behind; and the dislocation is not reset, for we can see it clearly and feel it well; and let it be dislocated according to each shape.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the dislocated shoulder with the sound one, so that you can see it openly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is chopped off, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it in such a way that the veins do not come out, for if the veins come out, then it would be grief to bring it back; and perhaps it cannot be brought back from all sides, most especially behind; and if this dislocation comes last, it is more painful than the others, and many die.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is thus, when it is such that she can be brought back, that you extend her hand to your two hands; and its arms are spread out, and the hands of his mirrour according to the knot around the neck, behind and in front, and press the joint to its skin together, or at the root of his palm, until it revives to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocations are in front, then come back when he doubles his hand to his hand, and be firm at the root of the palm where the loop has dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not return to its place, then give strong extension; and it is that two minister extend the arm, and dip two ministers, so that it does not move with the extension; then turn the arm of each part, then you have wrapped a double long and wide cloth; and when you look at the joint, if you rub it with any oil to soften the joint, then press the joint together, until he revives; and when he is in place, put on dry plaster with auburn of egg, and stretch it together, and tie the arm to the neck of the sick person, and leave it for some days, then loosen it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, let it be, and if you see that the joint is not well-joined, then begin to plaster and tie it, and leave it thus for some days, until it is firmly set; then remove it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the joint has been moved, and it moves, then bathe and gently rub it, and press until it is eased; or put wool fat on the joint, then leave it for a day and a night, then reset it, and let it enter or bath; and when it sweats, gently rub the joint, then put the wool fat on again, and then enter or bathe; and do this II times or III, until it is well; and if you see, then put raw sheep's fat that has been heated with butter on it, and strain it over; so it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand is less stable than that of other joints, and should be reset as soon as possible while still dislocated, so that the joint swells or an abscess develops.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And when you reset the hand, let the patient place his injured hand on a tray, and extend his fingers, and make sure his palm is facing the joint's alignment, like this, so that it can move freely while still being reset; then check if it is in the right position; finally, let him put his injured hand on a tray to be extended and reset.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	If the dislocation is at the back of the hand, let the patient place his hand on a tray with his palm facing the joint's alignment.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that's good; but if not, let him extract the pustules and poultices gently and leave it in that condition without encouraging reinfection.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	If he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after some days, then the joint is twisted; and there is no benefit to the patient except that his hands are moistened, and he cannot extract anything at all: therefore know that the nerve is cut, or the artery; if there is another reason for this besides extracting with a delicate cautery, and by chance there is nothing else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	When the hand is in place, put the poultice on it as we have said, then extract and leave it for V days, then remove it and leave it.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he cannot move it well, and there is no injury, if the warm water moistens it and he rubs it until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	the dislocation of the two joints in the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	de la dislocation des deux joints dans la main
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	Do they remove the scalp of the man from his head?
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the hair of the head or the neck is removed, or many are removed, there will be no cure for the patient, because death comes quickly to the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the exudations have come out without will, they cannot be held back, and many times a limb is weakened, or the II feet or the two arms or one; and many times the hair at the back moves in four directions; what moves from behind is called 'gilbositez': if it comes from childhood there is no cure for the whole: if not, there will be no healing.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from sitting down or striking or similar things, the ancient ways of curing them with great words did not bring much benefit, but I have shortened it according to my intention, and I have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the case of a broken leg, there is no cure; and also what comes straight into the two sides, and can only be properly cured who comes to the back, as I said; and it is so that the patient should lie on his face in one place, and have a bandage tied tightly around him, so he does not hurt himself; then take a twig of fire and form it into a stick, and another at the feet, and tie a piece of cloth around the leg, and another at the ankles, and two ministers should hold the bands, one at the head and one at the feet, between the two sticks; and they should be firmly tied, as we have said, and the fire-stick put its palms on the spine, until it heals.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if this cure does not work, take a big stick three arms long, and chop off the back wall with it, and let the patient lie on one side, and knock the head of the patient against the side of the table, then put the middle of the table on the spine; and place the minister's hands on the other head of the table, and press hard, until he comes back to his position; and if you see that it hurts, do it at a twist that twists the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And it is that you put II torches in the head of the patient with an arm from a tree, and between each torch, back and forth, a palm of space long; and in each torch, a hole, or the turn returns, and are the torches firmly in the ground so that they do not move, and between each pair of torches there is a turning torch, for by doing so the tie turns, and there are II small torches a palm long, to return the turner; and then lie the bond which is among the hands to the turner towards the head, and the other bond towards the teeth on the other turner, and each of the ministers turns his turner on all the bond, and the master puts the spine equal as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is equal, put it on a desiccated plaster with abundant ash, and then the stones, and then the tablet of III fingers long, that by pure his place of the gibbosity and the part of the spine healthy, then tie it with a string as we have said, and use subtle fasting on the patient until he is healthy; and if in the end of the health comes, then administer medicines softening and soothing, with the tablet that we have said before; and never give him a piece of lead, and never comes the appearance behind the spine of the back, and take care that this is dislocations; and this is the bone that opens, for by adventure might come death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of the hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	That the joints of the hip and shoulder come only from dislocations, not otherwise, but rather as for the other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to IV parties: inside and outside, front and back; and more inside, and less in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocations inside is that when one joins the leg with the sick, it is more long and higher than the healthy genitals, and cannot double the sick knee; and is the position which is swollen hot of an abscess, because of this the head of the thigh comes out.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of that one which comes to the outside, it is that this accident is opposite to these before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of that one which comes to the front, it is that his leg is well arranged according to the achievement; nevertheless, it does not double the knee with pain, and if he is made to walk, it cannot go forward, and holds back its urine, and swells up the ankle, and when he walks, it goes on the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of that which is behind him, if it is that he cannot spread his knee, nor double over, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the hip is softened, and the head of the thigh is out of place at the side of the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	And the signs of that which is behind him, if it is that he cannot spread his knee, nor double over, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the hip is softened, and the head of the thigh is out of place at the side of the ribs. If this dislocation has been there before and does not stay in place according to its disposition, then there is no cure for it; and it only comes from presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in that one whose dislocation is fresh, and it is of the four ways of dislocation, if you hasten to turn the joint, and make it move inward and outward, and to the right and left; perhaps it will come back, and there is no need for any other cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if he does not return in this way, it is necessary that you prepare the minister strongly, and hold the leg strongly with two hands, or with one thong that is tied to the knee; and extend another minister his hand above in such a manner that he presses his hands against his sides, then tie him down with a thong on the buttocks; and stretch another one's head of the thong; and they extend upward and downward all at once, so that the patient is raised from the ground all at once, and remains still.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This way of extension is common to four resemblances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, it is necessary to put the cure on his back, then put the thong on the root of the buttocks, and the line that is out of place, then extend the thong above towards the anus, and towards the force; and another minister should grasp his arms, and embrace the large line of the buttocks of the patient, and extend it to one side: so he will return to his place now; and this way of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	Et if you cannot do this in the way that we have said, it is necessary to tie together the two feet of the sick person with a strong rope under his heels and on his knees, and let the sick leg be extended more than the other; then hang him by the head on a pole, and place two long arms above the ground; and command the minister that he embrace the chief of the chest, and let other ministers hang with the sick person who embraces the chest properly, for the joints now come together again with care.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And if the dislocations are far away, so lay the sick person down as we have said in that which has gibbosity, and remove the rope properly from the sick leg, and also from the foot; then put two torches, one at the head and one at the feet, then place one torch between the legs of the sick person in the form; and let there be placed wet tapestries around, so that they do not burn the sick person, then spread each minister out before him, and let the doctor put his hand on the dislocation equally.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it comes back, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place it on a table, and press it in as we have said in the gibosity, and lay the patient on the left side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, if it is convenient to extend the leg of the patient in bed, and according to what I have said; and put the mirrour upon his pain to be under the armpit of the diseased leg, then press with the other hand, and turn it downward towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is on the far side, so it is not convenient to extend the leg of the patient in bed, do not raise him up from the ground, but rather that he be placed as if his hip was dislocated on the far side, as we have said above in the laying down on two hips; and let him lie on his face, and extend the bandage so as to press it on the joint at the table; and will be complete when the patient extends his legs, and they are even; then tie them up, and put the plaster on, and draw out a bandage, so that the hip does not move; and let him rest for three or four days, then take off the plaster, and make him go over, so as to even the members.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	is displaced within and beyond, and behind; and does not dislocate in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	is displaced within and beyond, and behind; and does not dislocate in front. The signs that this is the case are that you order the patient to bend his knee to his shin, and if he doesn't do so at his shin, know that he is displaced; and the restoration of all this is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back on his face, and place his foot on your toes; then take his knee between your palms, and pull apart the two knees at the knee joint; and other ministers extend his foot, until the knee has returned to its place, and the signs are that he is bending his leg to his shin lightly; and put the plaster on, and make him move his leg to the shin, and join them together firmly for three days or four, then take it off. And you do not work at moving the patient until the members have become comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limbs are not in place, let there be a strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until they are healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation from the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are never dislocated, nor completely dislocated inward or outward.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is dislocated, and turn before to the part where it is dislocated: one should bring it gently to their hands when it is only slightly dislocated.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated from the top, so that you make the patient sit upright, and support the leg under the ankle; then turn the foot to your right hand, and then to your left hand twice, and then extend it upward, and blow strongly on the foot; and do this twice, as we have said, in turning and blowing: if it returns, it is well; if not, then recommence the work, for it will return; and if it cannot return, so make the patient lie down on his back on the ground, and place a staff firmly between his thighs, and tie the bandages around, so that he does not fall; then support the leg with one minister, and other ministers extend the foot in their hands or at their sides, that he may lie upon the staff of col; then each minister extends equally, and the staff is kept in place between the patient's thighs to hold him down while you are supporting him; then put the bandages equally around the dislocation with your hands, and other ministers support the healthy leg under the ankle, and the dislocation will return completely.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is well-healed, then apply the plaster and press it on, and the bandage forms, and fasten the leg to the foot, and hold back the tendons behind the ankle so that the bonds are not too tight; then leave it for two days or three, and the bonds will become looser if the bandage; then release it after three days or four, and let the patient walk after four days. And if he goes before this term, it is not yet certain that he has dislocated it again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses develop, then you must calm them down, as we have said elsewhere, as long as they are healthy.
des dois	of the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, then it is easily repaired without work, and it is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in the back of the foot, then you must make the patient sit on a flat surface or a table completely upright, and place your foot on what opens up from these joints, then press it down with the foot forming, until it has healed; and when it has healed, and there is no opening, then put a splint on the foot of a table at two joints, then bandage it, and let it free; and let it rest, until it is healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and you want to restore it, many times the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in the treatment, unless you are skilled in this art and have practiced it for a long time; and do not be harsh, but use gentle heat at first, and leave the patient to God; if you see hope of health, then immediately set the member back into place, so that the abscesses come to a head; and when the member is back in its place, administer dry things to the abscesses, and treat the wound as needed with ointments; and if there is fracture and broken bones, do what we have said for simple diseases; and guard against entering a path of fear, as I have said, because that will cost you dear according to your Creator, and for the sake of arming yourself and your body.
Amen	Amen
